From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jan  1 13:24:37 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Bob Paddock)
Date: Tue, 1 Jan 2002 08:24:37 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Configuring your Web server to handle the DjVu MIME Types
Message-ID: <200201010822640.SM00191@there>

DjVu is a new file format becoming popular for posting scanned documents to 
web sites.  For example one document I just dealt with was 520K as DjVu and 
3.6 Megs as a PDF.

Check out:
http://www.djvuzone.org/

http://any2web.djvuzone.org/

http://openlib.djvuzone.org/

Now my question is how do I get xitami to serve these DjVu file types?

I added these to xitami.cfg:
    #   Image MIME types
    djv=image/x.djvu
    djvu=image/x.djvu

Can I put those in default.cfg or must mime types be in xitami.cfg?

However they don't seem to show up when I restart the server from the /admin 
screen.  I did back all the way up to the first screen like one of the 
recent messages said to do.

Xitami wants to download rather than serve the files.

Info on how to do this for Apache:

If you get garbled output when attempting to view DjVu documents
from your web page using Netscape, it means your web server
software is not configured to serve the DjVu mime.types.
The bib2web server automatically includes a hidden file named .htaccess
in the output TAR/ZIP file. This hidden file tells your web server
to serve .djvu files with the image/x.djvu mime.type.
However, certain types of web servers do not recognize this file,
in which case you must ask your system administrator to
configure your web server to serve DjVu files properly.

If your Web server runs the Apache web server, please follow the instructions 
below. If your server runs another Web server than Apache, please visit  
http://djvuzone.org/support/tutorial/chapter-serving.html#mime2
for instructions on how to configure it to serve DjVu documents.

Configuring Apache to serve DjVu documents.
login as root
 
Using a text editor, edit the file mimes.types file 
     used by your Web server (generally /etc/mime.types) 
     and add to following line to it:
              image/x.djvu djvu djv

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jan  1 15:03:49 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Tue, 01 Jan 2002 16:03:49 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] FTP problems
Message-ID: <46235@dsl.co.uk>

In message <200112280919.WAA09230@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>
   Ewen McNeill writes:
> In message <7DF4D412-FB6E-11D5-949F-0003933D8C18@mac.com>, Bruce Axtens writes:
> >On Friday, December 28, 2001, at 04:04  PM, Ewen McNeill wrote:
> >> Don't use FTP.  Use HTTP.  It's much cleaner.)
> >
> >Pardon my newbie-ness but, like, how?
> 

[snip some "why HTTP is superior to FTP" advocacy]

> FTP has no reliable way to return date/time meta information about
> files; each FTP client "guesses" this information from directory
> listings, after having guessed what the directory listing format is.
> HTTP specifically includes this information in its answer.  HTTP has a
> "get if modified" request; the equivilent in FTP involves getting a
> directory listing, guessing the format, guessing the details of the
> file, comparing it with what you have, and hoping for the best.
> 
> There's plenty more.  But basically FTP was designed by a bunch of grad
> students 20-something years ago making it up as they went along to solve
> a much more general problem than was really required, in an environment
> security and firewalls weren't an issue.  HTTP was designed more
> recently (about 10 years ago), and is much more firewall friendly.

Apart from the more-firewall-friendly aspect, I feel that you are being
more than a little unfair on both FTP and its implementors.
(Particularly in referring to Jon Postel as a "grad student".)

Might I remind you of the following (from RFC-1123, dated October 1989)?

         The File Transfer Protocol FTP is the primary Internet standard
         for file transfer.  The current specification is contained in
         RFC-959 [FTP:1].

         FTP uses separate simultaneous TCP connections for control and
         for data transfer.  The FTP protocol includes many features,
         some of which are not commonly implemented.  However, for every
         feature in FTP, there exists at least one implementation.  The
         minimum implementation defined in RFC-959 was too small, so a
         somewhat larger minimum implementation is defined here.

         Internet users have been unnecessarily burdened for years by
         deficient FTP implementations.  Protocol implementors have
         suffered from the erroneous opinion that implementing FTP ought
         to be a small and trivial task.  This is wrong, because FTP has
         a user interface, because it has to deal (correctly) with the
         whole variety of communication and operating system errors that
         may occur, and because it has to handle the great diversity of
         real file systems in the world.

It was RFC-1123 (aka STD-3), incidentally, which first standardized
certain extensions to FTP, such as PASV.  There are also more recent RFCs
which amplify 959, including at least three which have the status of
"proposed standard".

>> There's plenty more.  But basically FTP was designed by a bunch of grad
>> students 20-something years ago making it up as they went along to solve
>> a much more general problem than was really required, in an environment
>> security and firewalls weren't an issue.  
>
>Apart from the more-firewall-friendly aspect, I feel that you are being
>more than a little unfair on both FTP and its implementors.
>(Particularly in referring to Jon Postel as a "grad student".)

Well he was a grad student :-)  (At least in the early 1980s when FTP
was first being invented; the later RFCs/standards simply consolidated
things somewhat.)

Some of the generality of FTP was useful once (such as translating from
old IBM mainframes to ASCII based systems and such like), but much of it
has outlived its usefulness.  That combined with the fact that FTP and
firewalls badly disagree with each other means that I'd be pretty happy
to see FTP go away for good.

Ewen

>  how do I get xitami to serve these DjVu file types?

> Xitami wants to download rather than serve the files.

I think it would be correct to say your _browser_ wants to
download the file. Either way, Xitami is offering to serve the
file... your browser either knows what to do (and most browsers
don't know what Djvu is) or save it for you to deal with later.

Have you installed a Djvu reader in your browser? Do you expect
all your surfers to already have Djvu support? 

The standard technique seems to be to use EMBED to force download
of a reader that knows what Djvu is; see: 

http://www.djvuzone.org/support/tutorial/chapter-authoring2.html

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jan  2 15:46:38 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Hugo Notti)
Date: Wed, 2 Jan 2002 16:46:38 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] HTML using Perl
References: <sc3033c4.017@co.broward.fl.us>
Message-ID: <001a01c193a4$ab190db0$0201a8c0@dieter>

For escape characters:

"\n" is not recognized by any browser because it is perl-syntax, not html.
The same applies for other escapes.

If you use

print "I want this\nand another line";

you will get one line in the browser but two lines in the source code (as
seen from the browser).

In order to have two lines, you have to use

print "I want this<br>and another line";

which will be one line in source code but two lines in the browser.

Best regards,

Hugo
----- Original Message -----
From: "TOM MCGOVERN" <TMCGOVERN@broward.org>
To: "<" <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
Sent: Monday, December 31, 2001 3:45 PM
Subject: [Xitami] HTML using Perl


Hello Folks,

Why is it that the "\n"  and other escape characters in my Perl script are
not being recognized in the IOExplorer browser?? I start the html code with
the prescribed  .....print "Content-type: text/html\n\n";..... I'm running
Win NT 4.0 and perl5 and IOExplorer 5.5.

By the way, after much pain and suffering, I discovered from this Q&A list
that I had to include the ".pl=application/x-http-perl" statement in the
Mime section and "pl=C:\perlpath\perl.exe" in the Filter section of the
Defaults.cfg file in order to get my NT 4.0 to execute the Perl5 script.
Thanks for that.

Regards to all!

This works for me:

<link rel="SHORTCUT ICON" href="http://www.gwerx.com/images/gwerx.ico">
<link rel="BOOKMARK" href="http://www.gwerx.com/images/gwerx.ico">

Forget the "favicon.ico". Apparently, the "favicon" part is just for
promotional purposes. You can substitute it with "anything".

I hope this helps.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan  4 02:53:20 2002

I program Visual Basic and Macromedia Shockwave Director. 
I used to use ASP for stuff. 
Now I'm doing more CGI for communication when I want to read the server.
For posting to the server (from Shockwave)  ... I send an email to the server with the data encrypted.
A robot on my mail server unencrypts the email and posts data accordingly.
I like this because I can buffer a lot of heavy traffic on the email server,
and take my time doing the post. Plus I know I can't get hacked.
The robot has permissions into the database, but the email server can't see it.



I don't know a thing about Perl.
Dreamweaver is going to build your front end. I don't know about it's ability to build CGI scripts.

To build forms and corresponding CGI scripts in PERL, I saw this site. Haven't checked it
out ...    
http://www.munica.com/

Assuming you are on a windows platform (I think so) then the only thing 
you need is Perl itself. I use activestate perl latest whatever version 
and xitami on both Linux and windows and it all works wonderfully.

Occasionally you will find a perl script that barfs, generally because 
it has an expectation of Unix/Linux and/or Apache (e.g. I saw one that 
tried to look for .htaccess files), but they are rare and generally 
there are alternatives that aren't so badly written.

Francis

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan  4 21:12:05 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 05 Jan 2002 10:12:05 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] CGI
In-Reply-To: Message from Bruce <bd4u@earthlink.net>
 of "Fri, 04 Jan 2002 14:33:36 CDT." <so0c3uckqb06vb554nf64onf4pc6vt8gpc@4ax.com>
Message-ID: <200201042112.KAA15228@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <so0c3uckqb06vb554nf64onf4pc6vt8gpc@4ax.com>, Bruce writes:
>Does Xitami have ALL necessary software built into it to handle CGI scripts?

What do you mean by "ALL"?  It doesn't have half a dozen language
interpreters built in if that is what you are getting at.

Xitami does support most common CGI programs, although it has onlimited
non-parsed-header support, and it doesn't support flushing output to the
client before the end of the CGI run.  There are also reports that some
variable definitions are different from what is expected.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan  4 21:32:43 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 04 Jan 2002 16:32:43 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] CGI
References: <so0c3uckqb06vb554nf64onf4pc6vt8gpc@4ax.com>
Message-ID: <3C361F7B.E27822EC@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Does Xitami have ALL necessary software built into it to handle CGI scripts?

CGI is just a thin specification for an interface between a webserver and an
external program. It does NOT specify what that external program IS, so the
answer to your question is "No". 

I have CGI scripts written in DOS BAT file, and Visual Basic. unix shell
scripting is popular, but only on unix machines. There's also REXX and AWK and
one that sounds like a snake. 

The most popular tool for scripting today must be Perl, which as Francis said
you'll have to get and install. (Perl is much bigger and more often updated
than Xitami so it makes no sense to include Perl in an Xitami download.)

 -PRR

B>    I'm just trying to find out what options already
B> come with xitami, if I don't absolutely need Perl,
B> I'd like to know what my other options are. I'm NO
B> expert on computer languages (scripts), and the 
B> fewer I NEED to know at this point the better.

Basicly, xitami can run with any scripting language you want so comes
with all options. The catch is: you have to install the tool of your
choice yourself.

For example for the scripting language PHP (which you can get for free
at  www.php.net), you would just need to explain xitami to run php.exe
with all files which end with '.php', but only after you installed the
php.exe, of course...

Installing computer(scripting)languages is out of the scope of the
xitami manual. Refer to the computerlanguage of your choice to find
out how to install it on your system.

-- 
Best regards,
 Melle

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jan  9 07:18:19 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marc Doigny)
Date: Wed, 09 Jan 2002 08:18:19 +0100

In-Reply-To: <snhc3ukgl4jrri8sopvm7ta567h5vcb8i7@4ax.com>
References: <200201050005.BAA03404@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>
 <200201050005.BAA03404@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>
Message-ID: <5.0.2.1.2.20020109080717.01c86520@190.190.190.1>

At 01:24 5/01/02, you wrote:
>On Fri, 04 Jan 2002 15:57:44 -0800, you wrote:
>
> >CGI written in VB works perfect.
>
>
>What about the VB kernal, does it need to be in the path
>in order for Xitami to run a CGI script written in VB? Or are
>U saying Xitami will handle the routines by itself?

CGI written in VB (visual basic i suppose) don't need a VB kernel, since 
the code is compiled (resulting in an exe file)
When a normal script (like a dos batch file) executes the command processor 
has to be loaded first, the source compiled line per line (every time your 
script is called) and the resulting commands executed.

btw vb is not that efficient when it comes to handling cgi: vb is written 
with forms and user interaction and other visual stuff in mind. When vb 
loads, a lot of unnessary ballast is loaded altogether. cgi handling is 
actually just plain text processing, no visual effects (that part is done 
by the client browser). Should try Power Basic Console Compiler.



Marc

regards to CGI.   All use about the same amount of memory and 
resources.  VB uses standard nonvisual modules for this. There's

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jan  9 20:10:08 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Gunnar Swan)
Date: Wed, 09 Jan 2002 12:10:08 -0800
Subject: [Xitami] CGI
Message-ID: <200201092018.VAA21773@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>

By removing any and all forms from the VB project and using modules and classes ... you can get an EXE down to 28 - 32k that loads in a flash.

Yes, the VB virtual machine must also load. There are tools that allow you to keep these DLL's in memory, along with ADO.

This will provide even better response.

I only prefer VB because I've been programming in it for years. Of course ... there are other solutions, and VB is a Windows solution.

I'm not a MS freak, quite the contrary. I do Front end work in Shockwave. But for back end work, VB on an NT machine
running Xitami is quite nice.

Furthermore, I use VB and Director Shockwave EXE's as robots to read incoming emails.

I only use CGI for 'insecure' stuff ... stuff I don't care who sees.  For security, I encrypt emails and have robots read and decrypt the email content.

Very nice, all works quite well on the same server.  A 166 mhz Cyrix !

As I get bigger, I will put email server on another box, mySQL on another box and yet another box for the robots to execute.

ps. NT must be secured. Out the box it's insecure. 
Check out  O'Reilly Book " Securing Windows NT/2000 Servers"
ISBN : 1-56592-768-0

- - - -

time that some people from the second were not getting anything.

Norton Personal Firewall 2.0 with the latest and greatest.

Network settings. IP 192.168.1.5 subnet mask 255.255.255.0 - Gateway

turned things off such as FTP etc.

I do show them in the Wallwatcher log as an incoming connection and I do see
them as an active connection in the Xitami icon.

But for some reason the people on the second list do not get any pages
served to them.

I am by no means an expert in running a webserver but I do know a little. My
friend is an MSCE + Internet + a few others and he is stumped as to why this
is happening.
I have had someone at TZO try to do some testing remotely but they can't hit
the site or my computer either.

Any insight or a push in a certain direction to help me figure out the
problem will be greatly appreciated.

Thank you in advance for any help/direction you can provide.

Keith Hanley
www.hanleytime.com

  512 mb ram
  40 gb hard drive
  DSL connection through Earthlink/Mindspring. Handled by Covad.

  IE 6.0 128 bit encryption with all patches/updates from Microsoft =
site.

  Norton Antivirus 2000

  Network settings. IP 192.168.1.5 subnet mask 255.255.255.0 - Gateway =

   I got two suggestions.. 

1) ditch the firewall, you don't need it with Xitami, I tried using
sygates firewall, and all it did was get in the way.

2) Sprint will hook U up with a static IP, for $10 more a month plus
a small connection fee.

You might also wanna verify that your telephone lines are properly
grounded.



Best wishes

ITL, Bruce

  I apologize for the long email but I wanted to include as many details as
possible upfront.

   I am running a website (www.hanleytime.com) and am very happy with it
except for the fact that not everyone can connect. (view the website). It is
a family tree website so my traffic is very limited. I was using PWS but
didn't like the way it ran so I switched  to Xatami . My brother said it was
much faster using your software when he connected to my website.

  The following can connect at will.

  1. Friend using Roadrunner
  2. Mother using dialup
  3. Brother using dialup
  4. Myself locally
  5. From work using dialup

  The following cannot connect at any time. Ping and tracert do not work to
my site either.

  1. Friend using Roadrunner
  2. Sister using dialup
  3. From work using a T1
  4. Aunt using (not sure)
  5. TZO Tech Support

  I had people from the first list be able to view the website at the same
time that some people from the second were not getting anything.

  System details

  1.333 Ghz Althlon
  512 mb ram
  40 gb hard drive
  DSL connection through Earthlink/Mindspring. Handled by Covad.
  Linksys router (forwarding port 80 tcp to 192.168.1.5) I use Wallwatcher
to view the router log files.

  Windows 98 SE with all patches/updates from Microsoft site.
  IE 6.0 128 bit encryption with all patches/updates from Microsoft site.
  Norton Personal Firewall 2.0 with the latest and greatest.
  Norton Antivirus 2000
  TZO client
  Various family tree software

  Network settings. IP 192.168.1.5 subnet mask 255.255.255.0 - Gateway
192.168.1.1 (Linksys router) - DNS 207.69.188.186 and 207.69.188.185
(Mindspring DNS) Hostname - pongboy (my computer name)

  I have tested it with the firewall disabled and also uninstalled. Right
now it is installed since it didn't make any difference.

  I have uninstalled and reinstalled the Xitami software. It is a very easy
setup but not 100% sure that it is correct. I kept most of the defaults but
turned things off such as FTP etc.

  I do show them in the Wallwatcher log as an incoming connection and I do
see them as an active connection in the Xitami icon.

  But for some reason the people on the second list do not get any pages
served to them.

  I am by no means an expert in running a webserver but I do know a little.
My friend is an MSCE + Internet + a few others and he is stumped as to why
this is happening.
  I have had someone at TZO try to do some testing remotely but they can't
hit the site or my computer either.

  Any insight or a push in a certain direction to help me figure out the
problem will be greatly appreciated.

  Thank you in advance for any help/direction you can provide.

  Keith Hanley
  www.hanleytime.com

   I got two suggestions..

1) ditch the firewall, you don't need it with Xitami, I tried using
sygates firewall, and all it did was get in the way.

2) Sprint will hook U up with a static IP, for $10 more a month plus
a small connection fee.

You might also wanna verify that your telephone lines are properly
grounded.

    The following can connect at will.

    1. Friend using Roadrunner
    2. Sister using dialup
    3. From work using a T1
    4. Aunt using (not sure)
    5. TZO Tech Support

    I had people from the first list be able to view the website at the =
same time that some people from the second were not getting anything.

    System details

    1.333 Ghz Althlon
    512 mb ram
    40 gb hard drive
    DSL connection through Earthlink/Mindspring. Handled by Covad.
    Linksys router (forwarding port 80 tcp to 192.168.1.5) I use =
Wallwatcher to view the router log files.

    Windows 98 SE with all patches/updates from Microsoft site.
    IE 6.0 128 bit encryption with all patches/updates from Microsoft =
site.
    Norton Personal Firewall 2.0 with the latest and greatest.
    Norton Antivirus 2000
    TZO client
    Various family tree software=20

    Network settings. IP 192.168.1.5 subnet mask 255.255.255.0 - Gateway =
192.168.1.1 (Linksys router) - DNS 207.69.188.186 and 207.69.188.185 =
(Mindspring DNS) Hostname - pongboy (my computer name)=20

    I have tested it with the firewall disabled and also uninstalled. =
Right now it is installed since it didn't make any difference.

    I have uninstalled and reinstalled the Xitami software. It is a very =
easy setup but not 100% sure that it is correct. I kept most of the =
defaults but turned things off such as FTP etc.

    I do show them in the Wallwatcher log as an incoming connection and =
I do see them as an active connection in the Xitami icon.

    But for some reason the people on the second list do not get any =
pages served to them.

    I am by no means an expert in running a webserver but I do know a =

as to why this is happening.
    I have had someone at TZO try to do some testing remotely but they =

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)

Message-ID: <3C3CDCDB.E4995222@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Is a static ip necessary? I use TZO

Nice but not necessary. Using TZO to associate your name address to your
hopping IP number will give momentary glitches, but works well for many
people. 

In particular: if someone hits right after your IP number changes, they won't
connect until TZO gets updated. Since you say "checks it once a minute", that
should never leave you invisible for long.

A bigger issue, and I am not sure how this works, is that various ISPs may
cache DNS records on their own DNS servers rather than keep going to a DNS
server in authority. That's standard practice, the authoritative DNS record
can give a suggested time of updating, and I suppose TZO must be setting their
update suggestion shorter than a DNS system full of hard-wired "permanent IP"
machines like mine. But other ISP DNS servers are free to ignore it, and use
cached DNS records as long as they want. 

>  Ping and tracert 

By name, I assume. What happens if you call them on the phone, tell them the
IP number you are on at that moment, and they ping that number? i.e. is it a
DNS issue or is your IP number just not reachable? 

FWIW: ping 66.32.68.16 at 7:10 PM EST fails for me; tracert stops tracking
after three hops inside MindSpring. Omitting known route through my campus
routers and my usual ALTER.NET backbone routers:

 16    195.ATM4-0.GW6.ATL3.ALTER.NET [146.188.233.217]
 17    foundry-86-p3-2.atl2.mindspring.net [157.130.29.194]
 18    foundry-22-ve3.atl2.mindspring.net [207.69.223.163]
 19    redback-1-e2-0.atl2.mindspring.net [207.69.143.4]
 20     *        *        *     Request timed out.
 21     *        *        *     Request timed out.
 22     *        *        *     Request timed out.
 23     *        *        *     Request timed out.
 24     *        *        *     Request timed out.
 25     *     ^C

 -PRR

    I apologize for the long email but I wanted to include as many details
as possible upfront.

     I am running a website (www.hanleytime.com) and am very happy with it
except for the fact that not everyone can connect. (view the website). It is
a family tree website so my traffic is very limited. I was using PWS but
didn't like the way it ran so I switched  to Xatami . My brother said it was
much faster using your software when he connected to my website.

    The following can connect at will.

    1. Friend using Roadrunner
    2. Mother using dialup
    3. Brother using dialup
    4. Myself locally
    5. From work using dialup

    The following cannot connect at any time. Ping and tracert do not work
to my site either.

    1. Friend using Roadrunner
    2. Sister using dialup
    3. From work using a T1
    4. Aunt using (not sure)
    5. TZO Tech Support

    I had people from the first list be able to view the website at the same
time that some people from the second were not getting anything.

    System details

    1.333 Ghz Althlon
    512 mb ram
    40 gb hard drive
    DSL connection through Earthlink/Mindspring. Handled by Covad.
    Linksys router (forwarding port 80 tcp to 192.168.1.5) I use Wallwatcher
to view the router log files.

    Windows 98 SE with all patches/updates from Microsoft site.
    IE 6.0 128 bit encryption with all patches/updates from Microsoft site.
    Norton Personal Firewall 2.0 with the latest and greatest.
    Norton Antivirus 2000
    TZO client
    Various family tree software

    Network settings. IP 192.168.1.5 subnet mask 255.255.255.0 - Gateway
192.168.1.1 (Linksys router) - DNS 207.69.188.186 and 207.69.188.185
(Mindspring DNS) Hostname - pongboy (my computer name)

    I have tested it with the firewall disabled and also uninstalled. Right
now it is installed since it didn't make any difference.

    I have uninstalled and reinstalled the Xitami software. It is a very
easy setup but not 100% sure that it is correct. I kept most of the defaults
but turned things off such as FTP etc.

    I do show them in the Wallwatcher log as an incoming connection and I do
see them as an active connection in the Xitami icon.

    But for some reason the people on the second list do not get any pages
served to them.

    I am by no means an expert in running a webserver but I do know a
little. My friend is an MSCE + Internet + a few others and he is stumped as
to why this is happening.
    I have had someone at TZO try to do some testing remotely but they can't
hit the site or my computer either.

    Any insight or a push in a certain direction to help me figure out the
problem will be greatly appreciated.

    Thank you in advance for any help/direction you can provide.

    Keith Hanley
    www.hanleytime.com

-----Original Message-----
From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org
[mailto:xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org]On Behalf Of Paul Reid
Sent: Wednesday, January 09, 2002 7:14 PM
To: xitami@lists.xitami.org

> Is a static ip necessary? I use TZO

Nice but not necessary. Using TZO to associate your name address to your
hopping IP number will give momentary glitches, but works well for many
people.

In particular: if someone hits right after your IP number changes, they
won't
connect until TZO gets updated. Since you say "checks it once a minute",
that
should never leave you invisible for long.

A bigger issue, and I am not sure how this works, is that various ISPs may
cache DNS records on their own DNS servers rather than keep going to a DNS
server in authority. That's standard practice, the authoritative DNS record
can give a suggested time of updating, and I suppose TZO must be setting
their
update suggestion shorter than a DNS system full of hard-wired "permanent
IP"
machines like mine. But other ISP DNS servers are free to ignore it, and use
cached DNS records as long as they want.

>  Ping and tracert

By name, I assume. What happens if you call them on the phone, tell them the
IP number you are on at that moment, and they ping that number? i.e. is it a
DNS issue or is your IP number just not reachable?

FWIW: ping 66.32.68.16 at 7:10 PM EST fails for me; tracert stops tracking
after three hops inside MindSpring. Omitting known route through my campus
routers and my usual ALTER.NET backbone routers:

 16    195.ATM4-0.GW6.ATL3.ALTER.NET [146.188.233.217]
 17    foundry-86-p3-2.atl2.mindspring.net [157.130.29.194]
 18    foundry-22-ve3.atl2.mindspring.net [207.69.223.163]
 19    redback-1-e2-0.atl2.mindspring.net [207.69.143.4]
 20     *        *        *     Request timed out.
 21     *        *        *     Request timed out.
 22     *        *        *     Request timed out.
 23     *        *        *     Request timed out.
 24     *        *        *     Request timed out.
 25     *     ^C

 -PRR

Are you sure you're using php3 ??? php3 has been out of date for a LONG time
now; if so maybe you should download & install php4 (php.exe & friends) from
www.php.net. Also make sure that your system PATH variable contains the path to
the php.exe, perferably at the very beginning as Xitami seems to occasionally
have difficulty locating the main php dll if it is not on the path.

Paul


In c:\xitami\xitami.cfg I have the following section:

[Filter]
    .ssi=perlssi                        #   Pass *.ssi to PerlSSI
    .shtm=perlssi                       #   Pass *.shtm to PerlSSI
    .shtml=perlssi                      #   Pass *.shtml to PerlSSI
    .php=C:\PHP\php3.exe

I have php3.exe in C:\PHP.

When I go to a php document I get the following error:
Internal error: your request was unsuccessful
Cannot create CGI process - program not found

It seems to be saying it can't find php.exe!

Any ideas what I have missed?  I tried changing the reference to
c:\php\php3.exe in case there is case thing going on but it made no
difference.

By removing any and all forms from the VB project and using modules and classes
... you can get an EXE down to 28 - 32k that loads in a flash.

Yes, the VB virtual machine must also load. There are tools that allow you to
keep these DLL's in memory, along with ADO.

This will provide even better response.

I only prefer VB because I've been programming in it for years. Of course ...
there are other solutions, and VB is a Windows solution.

I'm not a MS freak, quite the contrary. I do Front end work in Shockwave. But
for back end work, VB on an NT machine
running Xitami is quite nice.

Furthermore, I use VB and Director Shockwave EXE's as robots to read incoming
emails.

I only use CGI for 'insecure' stuff ... stuff I don't care who sees.  For
security, I encrypt emails and have robots read and decrypt the email content.

Very nice, all works quite well on the same server.  A 166 mhz Cyrix !

As I get bigger, I will put email server on another box, mySQL on another box
and yet another box for the robots to execute.

ps. NT must be secured. Out the box it's insecure.
Check out  O'Reilly Book " Securing Windows NT/2000 Servers"
ISBN : 1-56592-768-0

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 10 01:48:03 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Gunnar Swan)
Date: Wed, 09 Jan 2002 17:48:03 -0800
Subject: [Xitami] CGI
Message-ID: <200201100156.CAA27616@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>

Sure. I use  IA mail server (on same box as Xitami) ... www.tnsoft.com
I write an EXE that can accept command line parameters, explained in a moment.
When a mail comes into a specific 'robot' email account, the mail server writes the email content to the hard drive and starts the EXE, providing as a parameter the 
path to the email file it just wrote.

After that, it's a matter of permissions and what you want to do with the email.
In this case, I have remote programs (clients) that via code ... send the email to a specific email address.
My robots ... EXE's .. unencrypt the data and based on the structure of the data, post the data to the 
database and send confirmation emails .

Advantage 1 ... The server ( 166 mhz Cyrix) can access 250 messages in 15 seconds without barking.  The messages are cached and stored until the contents are 
executed.

Advantage 2 ... The data sits encrypted in the mail message. Even if hacked, the contents are useless to intruders.

Advantage 3 ... The robots are run sequentially and can take their time.

Advantage 4 ... The robots can actually execute on another machine and 'poll' for new messages. With this technique, I can build a transaction processing system.

Works for me.  I use CGI, but not to post data. Only to read content from a relational database and run the queries on the server.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 10 02:06:29 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (evan heller)
Date: Wed, 09 Jan 2002 21:06:29 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] FW: Website using Xitami
References: <ldkp3uk4lpvb9gk1647ulb9qbgh9gmrdr1@4ax.com> <NFBBKPLALCNBMMILFGEJEEOBCBAA.spyman@mindspring.com> <b4rp3us6oie0fknglinvvkh4bc3j5qmm5h@4ax.com>
Message-ID: <3C3CF725.615AE0E2@alum.rpi.edu>

Ok, a few things here:

First off you should always have a firewall ESPECIALLY if your on a broadband
connection. My suggestion the freeware ZoneAlarm (www.zonealarm.com)  is both
easy to use and install.

Second, I use both dynamic ip addresses on my server as well as my server not
being dedicated and it acts JUST fine.

I use ZoneEdit (www.zoneedit.com) and the DirectUpdate engine for updating
the ip address. There have been no problems OTHER than the fact that most
isp's block port 80, forcing me to redirect all port 80 traffic to port 4080
which I accomplished easily using ZonEedit.

Now, as far as the speed of xitami is concerned, yes it's fast but a fast
webserver gets easily bogged down once you start to add things like PHP,
MySQL or ASP emulation. So depending on how much use you are getting out of
it and how fast your dsl is, it better to be safe than sorry.

Just my 2 cents.


-Evan

page.

Aren't one minute updates a bit obsessive?  Some Dynamic DNS services would 
ban you for doing that.  You should only need to do them when the link comes 
up.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 10 15:35:39 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Bruce)
Date: Thu, 10 Jan 2002 10:35:39 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] FW: Website using Xitami
In-Reply-To: <200201100859406.SM00388@there>
References: <NFBBKPLALCNBMMILFGEJCEOACBAA.spyman@mindspring.com> <ldkp3uk4lpvb9gk1647ulb9qbgh9gmrdr1@4ax.com> <200201100859406.SM00388@there>
Message-ID: <tsbr3ugdp7fhst4nqthb3jdreq2bn2mjt1@4ax.com>

On Thu, 10 Jan 2002 09:02:13 -0500, you wrote:

>
>> You might also wanna verify that your telephone lines are properly
>> grounded.
>
>Phone lines work on the principle of a balanced line transformer issolation 
>system, they should NEVER be grounded.  A grounded phone line will have a 
>very loud hum.
>
>I agree that the EQUIPMENT should be properly grounded, but not the phone 
>line.


   I'm not sure that we are talking about the same thing. I'm refering
to the outside lines, not the inside lines. The ones that come in to
the box from off the street. Simple test is pick up your phone
receiver and listen to it. If you here static, then U have a bad
ground. If while U talk to somebody U hear static the cause is a bad
ground more than likely. Like I said the connection coming into your
house, and not the inside line. There should be at least 3 feet of 3/8
inch copper rod driven into the ground for your telephone service
connection, properly secured and tightly fitted to a wire that leads
into your telephone box. If it's connected to a cold water pipe, or
something similar it can cause all kinds of comm problems.

   Since Sprint DSL comes in through your phone line, I can only
assume the same principle applies. I'm a technician, not an engineer
I work according to application, and not theory.

   Who knows, maybe I'm wrong, but then my phone lines, and DSL
work just fine. However, they didn't when I first bought the house
over 10 years ago. I had to have my box tested and serviced by
the tele-co before I got rid of the static. The reason for the test
was because I was using a modem, and was losing the connection
or getting gobbldy gook for IBM-ANSI characters all the time.

I hope this clarifies things..

ITL, Bruce

Are you sure you're using php3 ??? php3 has been out of date for a LONG time
now; if so maybe you should download & install php4 (php.exe & friends) from
www.php.net. Also make sure that your system PATH variable contains the path
to
the php.exe, perferably at the very beginning as Xitami seems to
occasionally
have difficulty locating the main php dll if it is not on the path.

Paul

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 10 18:00:54 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Control-Freak)
Date: Thu, 10 Jan 2002 13:00:54 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] FW: Website using Xitami
References: <NFBBKPLALCNBMMILFGEJCEOACBAA.spyman@mindspring.com> <200201100859703.SM00388@there>
Message-ID: <042501c19a00$c0095880$b61e2341@concentric.net>

I am not sure that the problem is not much more simple than everyone has
made it, as it has been a couple of days since the original post, and I am
able to connect just fine.  I have had similar problems as I have had other
companies host my sites up until recently.  In trying to find a good
provider, I often moved my site.

I found DNS updating to be a long and slow process.  It always seemed that
within  2 days or so of pointing my Domain at a host IP, half of the
internet could connect to my site, and half couldn't.  It often took more
than 2 weeks before I could trace route my site from servers everwhere (you
can do this at www.tracert.com).

If you have just recently set up your server, and pointed your domain at
your dynamic ISP service, be patient.  I know its very frustrating.  Within
a couple of weeks everyone will probably be able to connect to your site.

Good Luck,

Jay Aldrich

It is 8:51 EST right now on Jan/10 and I just connected to your site using
Opera 5/Linux.  I think your actually problem is that your EMAIL icon is not
there.  Some browser hang on things like this.   Opera rendered the text
then

HTML Tidy to make sure it is following the standards of the World Wide Web
Consortium.  Fix up the errors it reports then see if people can get your
page.

http://sourceforge.net/projects/tidy/

> 5. TZO Tech Support

Aren't one minute updates a bit obsessive?  Some Dynamic DNS services would
ban you for doing that.  You should only need to do them when the link comes
up.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan 11 04:56:42 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (David B Kelso)
Date: Thu, 10 Jan 2002 22:56:42 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] Re: Xitami - Cold Fusion - Win2k
Message-ID: <20020110.230815.-1799057.3.xpresitnet@juno.com>

On Thu, 10 Jan 2002 20:27:06 -0800 Gordon Wong
<gordonw@interchange.ubc.ca> writes:

> Anybody know if Xifusion works to allow ColdFusion Server Pro and 
> Xitami to
> talk? 

Yep. You need to add it as a filter in xitami.cfg

Looks like this:

#  
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
_
#   FILTER configuration section                                         
    _
#                                                                        
    _
#   This section lets you define filter programs. To define a filter,    
    _
#   specify a file extension with a leading dot and the filter           
    _
#   command. The command may be with a full path, or without, if the     
    _
#   program is on the PATH.                                              
    _
                                                                         
    _
[Filter]                                                                 
    _
                                                                         
    _
.cfm=c:\cfusion\bin\XiFusion c:\cfusion\bin\cfml.exe                     
    _


Now if someone could only help me with my problem! :-)

Dave

fire off an email to him at  thruska@css.tayloru.edu

I will not upgrade to Win2k unless you verify that the combination works, -
just in case.

Hello all. Hoping someone out there can give me a hand.

I am trying to transfer an entire web site to cdrom. Within the site there
are a few searches which basically open and parse data files, and then
dynamically generate html pages, using perl.

Can I do this with Xitami? I know that most any web server these days is
capable of cgi, including Xitami. But can it do it, having the web site,
xitami server and perl, all living on a cd, without tcpip?

I have tried this with MicroWeb and it works perfectly, but if tcp/ip is not
installed it doesn't work. I know what you are thinking -- "Who DOESN'T have
TCP/IP installed these days?" Unfortunately we can't insist that the 350,000
potential users of this cd have tcp/ip installed. Many wouldn't even know
what it is, let alone why they need it to browse a cd ...

Any help *MUCH* appreciated!

Bob

Have you configured Xitami to think that "/scripts/" indicates your
cgi-bin directory?  If not, then it'll never try to run the program,
and just send it to the browser.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan 11 12:18:18 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 12 Jan 2002 01:18:18 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Xitmami / cdrom / No network or TCPIP?
In-Reply-To: Message from "Robert Bowen" <robert.bowen@mubimedia.com>
 of "Fri, 11 Jan 2002 10:55:28 BST." <COEAJMCINDEAAHLGNCEMGEBACDAA.robert.bowen@mubimedia.com>
Message-ID: <200201111218.BAA11274@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <COEAJMCINDEAAHLGNCEMGEBACDAA.robert.bowen@mubimedia.com>, "Robert Bo
wen" writes:
>I am trying to transfer an entire web site to cdrom.  [Some dynamic
>content] But can it do it, having the web site, xitami server and perl, 
>all living on a cd, without tcpip?

No.  Xitami, and pretty much every other webserver I'm aware of uses
tcp/ip as it's transport protocol, and hence won't work if it isn't
installed.

ISTR that Dr Dobbs did something a year or two back with a Java applet
that did the searching which would work without a webserver, for much
this sort of context.  Might be worth digging around their site to see
if you can find anything.

If you can live with Windows only it may be possible to do something
with an ActiveX control.

Then again I'm not even sure it is possible to install a web browser
like IE or Netscape without TCP/IP installed.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

>Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com
You can make a cd rom that start window internet explorer automatically and 
loads an index page. (TCP/IP is not needed since only local files are accessed)
 From there on the users can navigate the CD like a normal internet site.
It will not be possible to execute programs, but IE has a FIND function.
There are also javascripts commands that let you select records in a file. 
Normally these commands are not used in an internet environment, since the 
whole file has to be downloaded anyway, but they function well for local 
browsing.

I regularly distribute CD-ROMS that way, and i never had complains that the 
files could not be read.
Of course the CD-ROM will only be accessible by windows PC's.

Simply make a "autorun.inf" file in the root of the CD with following content:

[autorun]
open=start index.htm

(assuming index.htm is also in the root of the CD)


Marc

Robert Bowen wrote:

>Hello all. Hoping someone out there can give me a hand.
>
>I am trying to transfer an entire web site to cdrom. Within the site there
>are a few searches which basically open and parse data files, and then
>dynamically generate html pages, using perl.
>
>Can I do this with Xitami? I know that most any web server these days is
>capable of cgi, including Xitami. But can it do it, having the web site,
>xitami server and perl, all living on a cd, without tcpip?

As others have said this isn't really a web server problem its more a 
browser problem. If you were willing to investigate the possibility of 
distributing the mozilla browser on your CD then you could look at 
including protozilla as a way to run a kind of "client side" CGI. 
However I suspect its easier to assume a TCPIP stack.

If interested take a look at http://protozilla.mozdev.org/ and an 
article at http://linuxjournal.com/article.php?sid=4724&mode=thread&order=0

Also bear in mind this is definitely beta code at present

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan 11 15:52:21 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Pieter Hintjens)
Date: Fri, 11 Jan 2002 16:52:21 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Xitmami / cdrom / No network or TCPIP?
In-Reply-To: <COEAJMCINDEAAHLGNCEMGEBACDAA.robert.bowen@mubimedia.com>
Message-ID: <3C3F1845.25980.F4E9998@localhost>

"Robert Bowen" <robert.bowen@mubimedia.com> wrote:

> I am trying to transfer an entire web site to cdrom. Within the site
> there are a few searches which basically open and parse data files,
> and then dynamically generate html pages, using perl...

It's impossible to run a 'live' site with CGIs and Perl without 
TCP/IP.  However, you can probably make a CD-ROM that everyone can 
use if you bend the rules a little.

First, create a start page that is entirely static.  Anyone with a 
browser, with or without TCP/IP, will be able to access this.  If you 
have dynamic output on the first page, cheat by pregenerating 
something that will show without HTTP access.  Then, make as much of 
the site work in static HTML and make it clear that the rest of the 
site is only available to people who have TCP/IP installed (which is 
frankly trivial on all Windows platforms from 95 upwards, even if it 
simply means installing dial-up networking).

You will also need to start Xitami in the background.  You can 
probably do this using the autorun.inf file.

-
Pieter Hintjens
iMatix Corporation



From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan 11 16:09:24 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 11 Jan 2002 11:09:24 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] FW: Website using Xitami
References: <NFBBKPLALCNBMMILFGEJCEOACBAA.spyman@mindspring.com> <ldkp3uk4lpvb9gk1647ulb9qbgh9gmrdr1@4ax.com> <200201100859406.SM00388@there> <tsbr3ugdp7fhst4nqthb3jdreq2bn2mjt1@4ax.com>
Message-ID: <3C3F0E34.11AC928E@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Simple test is pick up your phone receiver and listen to it. If you here static, then U have a bad ground. 

It could be a lot of things. In any case, in the USA, phone grounding is the
PHONE COMPANY'S job, not the customer's job. If you hear hum or static, bypass
your inside wiring by plugging into the box where the phone line comes into
the house. (If you don't have the modern kind of telco entrance box, call the
phone company and demand one: they are very much better than the old carbon
block protectors, and easier to diagnose.) If you have hum inside but not at
the box, fix (preferably re-run) your inside wires. If you have hum at the
outside box, MAKE the telco fix it. There may be larger safety issues. 

> There should be at least 3 feet of 3/8 inch copper rod driven into the ground for your telephone 

A dirt rod, especially a little 3-foot, is almost worthless in most US soils.
It has a resistance as high as the phone line. A dirt rod is no longer allowed
to be a home's only power ground, and it isn't allowed for power and phone to
"share" a dirt rod (that becomes exceptionally dangerous in lightning or when
a 13,000/240 power transformer shorts). 

If that fixed your problems, I guess you better leave it alone. But I wouldn't
like it, my phone company would be upset, and the electrical inspector
probably should be consulted. Home grounding has become complex lately; the
best rule is "it is usually done wrong". 

> If it's connected to a cold water pipe, or something similar it can cause all kinds of comm problems.

Until plastic pipe became common, the water system was the same as a dirt rod
(it goes through the same dirt!) except VERY much better, being miles long and
typically wet from seepage in the mains. In my area, the telco always
connected to a metal water pipe: even had a standard clamp and "WARNING" tag
for the purpose. That should do no harm; though with modern plastic pipe it
may do no good. (My inside pipe is copper but I discovered that it turns to
plastic a foot outside the cellar, so I get no benefit from the water mains
system.) 

"Your" side of the telco entrance point should be UNgrounded. The wires
"should" be correctly grounded (through protector blocks which don't ground
the normal signals) by the telco. Most telcos are pretty good about this: if a
home phone is improperly grounded, THEIR workers are in danger. 

If you have static, call and complain. Many telcos don't want to hear about
modems, and may have lax standards for voice quality. But if you say you hear
static AND your fax machine prints garbage and drops the connection, they will
often do something about it. 

 -PRR

   "David Holm" writes:

> This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

Please DON'T do this: plain ASCII is perfectly adequate for mailing list
mails: no one wants to see the indetical content wrapped up in needless
swathes of HTML as well as the ASCII version.

So find the setting in your mailer that says "send messages as plain text
only".

> You seem to have more than one problem. Checking your DNS record I find =
> your site listed at 66.32.68.16 which is not correct from what you =
> state. Also when I ping the 192.168.1.5 I get returns from =
> 207.218.53.201 and cannot resolve the name through DNS of that IP. I am =
> an ISP connected direct to the internet through a T1 connection.

Duh!

You seem to have a problem too!  Addresses in the range [192.168.0.0] to
[192.168.255.255] are PRIVATE ones, which are explicitly not routable.
(See RFC-1918.)

If you're getting a reply to the ping, then YOUR network must have a
machine with the identity [192.168.1.5] --- it goes nowhere near Spyman's
system

You also have another problem, in that you've failed to excise anything
from Spyman's message: you ought to quote only sufficient to provide a
background for your reply, so really the precepts applicable to news will
work: <http://www.geocities.com/nnqweb/nquote.html> provides good
guidance on how to quote in news articles, and is a good paradigm for
mailing lists too.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan 11 23:14:47 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Warren 'Llama' Ernst)
Date: Fri, 11 Jan 2002 15:14:47 -0800
Subject: [Xitami] PHP - install issue and solution
In-Reply-To: <028701c199c2$8d6fbce0$d363e73f@patricko>
Message-ID: <NCBBKPOEGDDBEOIEHJLFIEGOCOAA.warren@warrenernst.com>

All,

I just installed PHP 4.1.0 on my Xitami box, and I was getting the same
errors as the previous posters of this thread had mentioned: some error
message in the browser window about not being able to find the executable.

Well, I found a solution that may be of help. When I tried to run a sample
script at the command line, I got an error dialog box which said it was
unable to locate obdc32.dll. I checked around for this file on another
machine, found it, copied it over to c:\windows\system (this is a win98 box)
and tried the sample script again. Now it complained about missing another
DLL (its name escapes me right now.) I also copied it over and tried the
sample script one more time.

Bingo!

A check on the PHP site for these missing dll files indicates that these
missing files can be a problem - not very common, but it does happen. Other
users reported installing the free version of MySQL solved the problem - it
must have the right DLLs.

Anyway, its all working now, and I'm ready to start learning PHP. I just
thought I would share my experience.

-Warr

> You will also need to start Xitami in the background.  You can

I've been this route, tho at the time I using TinyWeb, had not learned of 
Xitami yet.  I would never try to do this again, it didn't work.

People didn't understand that they needed this web server running.  Some 
programs thought that it was a virus, or a Back-Orfice kind of spy program.

Some one else complained about the resources that the server where being 
used.  Even when all of the software was removed they STILL complained that 
it was the web servers fault that their resources where low.

I ended up writing my own "browser" that would read the HTML files, using 
the wxWindows tool kit, http://www.wxwindows.org/ .  Every one seems happy 
with that.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan 11 20:35:09 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Fri, 11 Jan 2002 20:35:09
Subject: [Xitami] PHP - install issue and solution
In-Reply-To: <NCBBKPOEGDDBEOIEHJLFIEGOCOAA.warren@warrenernst.com>
References: <028701c199c2$8d6fbce0$d363e73f@patricko>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20020111203509.00a05d98@www.shininglightpro.com>

At 03:14 PM 1/11/2002 -0800, Warren 'Llama' Ernst writeth:
>All,
>
>I just installed PHP 4.1.0 on my Xitami box, and I was getting the same
>errors as the previous posters of this thread had mentioned: some error
>message in the browser window about not being able to find the executable.
>
>Well, I found a solution that may be of help. When I tried to run a sample
>script at the command line, I got an error dialog box which said it was
>unable to locate obdc32.dll. I checked around for this file on another
>machine, found it, copied it over to c:\windows\system (this is a win98 box)
>and tried the sample script again. Now it complained about missing another
>DLL (its name escapes me right now.) I also copied it over and tried the
>sample script one more time.
>
>Bingo!

Not 'Bingo'...doing that can cause *serious* problems and possibly even
destroy a working OS (even Linux can't stand up to changes like that if not
done properly and will crash if such changes are made foolishly).

The correct way to get the odbc32.dll (and other related drivers) onto your
system is to go to <http://www.microsoft.com/odbc/> and download the latest
ODBC drivers from there.  Be sure to update your Jet drivers (which you
probably don't have installed since ODBC isn't installed) as well in case
you ever do anything with databases.

Only in rare (and I mean *REALLY* rare) circumstances is copying DLLs a
good idea.  Most DLLs and applications need to be registered with the OS
via the registry.  Copying files over doesn't add the needed entries to the
registry and if you attempt to use any of the ODBC functions in PHP, PHP
will probably crash or will return garbage (and if it crashes, the system
will probably become unstable).

I highly recommend installing ODBC correctly to help keep your system stable.

Hope this helps!


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

<snip>

It appears that Xitami might not have permissions to access the file or
some sort of really bizarre firewall is preventing the data from going
through.  Now I'm not sure how Xitami does this, but it is possible to
attain file information without opening the file (verifies that it exists).
 So, the permissions might be set up such that Xitami can get the file
information (size, etc.) and return it but not be able to open and read the
file.

One other, however highly unlikely, possibility is a corrupt Xitami
installation (TCP/IP stack or OS installation?)

Hope this helps!


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jan 14 21:09:12 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 15 Jan 2002 10:09:12 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Content type for .CSS
In-Reply-To: Message from Melle Koning <hace_x@yahoo.com>
 of "Mon, 14 Jan 2002 21:48:39 BST." <691406214.20020114214839@chello.nl>
Message-ID: <200201142109.KAA10121@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <691406214.20020114214839@chello.nl>, Melle Koning writes:
>He suggests (in dutch): That's a strange content-type, shouldn't you
>set the content-type for .css to "text/css"
>
>I would like to, so how do I change content-type for .css in Xitami?

Add:

[Mime]
   css=text/css

to defaults.cfg and restart Xitami.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

>It appears that Xitami might not have permissions to access the file or
>some sort of really bizarre firewall is preventing the data from going
>through.  Now I'm not sure how Xitami does this, but it is possible to
>attain file information without opening the file (verifies that it exists).
> So, the permissions might be set up such that Xitami can get the file
>information (size, etc.) and return it but not be able to open and read the
>file.
>
>One other, however highly unlikely, possibility is a corrupt Xitami
>installation (TCP/IP stack or OS installation?)
>
>Hope this helps!
>
>
>           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
>Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
>                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/
>

custom digits, unlike link-to counters.  I have made digits in PaintShop
from GIF images and even from photo JPG images.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jan 16 14:05:56 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Craig Morrison)
Date: Wed, 16 Jan 2002 09:05:56 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] NOCC Mailer setup question
References: <LKBBKLDHICNIAKJMKNCEGELEDLAA.warren@warrenernst.com>
Message-ID: <3C4588C4.8FEA3124@2cah.com>

Warren 'Llama' Ernst wrote:
> 
> Ignoring that url is spelled "uri", I'm not sure what this note means.

URI is a broader form, so it is correct.

> 
> I have the files located in c:\xitami\webpages\nocc, if that means anything.

Then that is what you set base_uri to:

  $base_uri = 'c:/xitami/webpages/nocc/';

Note, you may have to drop the trailing / I can't remember off-hand if it is
needed or not.

It is used for page redirection.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jan 16 18:05:56 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Wed, 16 Jan 2002 19:05:56 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] NOCC Mailer setup question
Message-ID: <46456@dsl.co.uk>

In message <LKBBKLDHICNIAKJMKNCEGELEDLAA.warren@warrenernst.com>
   "Warren 'Llama' Ernst" writes:
> I am trying to set up NOCC, a web based email PHP script.
> 
> It has a line in its configuration files that says:
> 
> // Base URL where NOCC is hosted (only needed for Xitami servers, see
> #463390)
> $base_uri = '';
> 
> 
> Ignoring that url is spelled "uri", I'm not sure what this note means.

It may NOT be misspelt: since 1994, the official terminology (see
RFC-1630) has been Universal Resource Identifier (URI), and /not/
Universal Resource Locator (URL).

Considering that probably more than 90% of the present-day users of the
Internet have come to it since that date, it's surprising that everyone
uses a term that was already officially obsolete when they joined.  I
suspect that we must blame those responsible for programs such as
Nutscrape & Internet Exploder who did nothing to promulgate the official
nomenclature.

-- 
Brian {Hamilton Kelly}                                          bhk@dsl.co.uk
    "We have gone from a world of concentrated knowledge and wisdom to one of
    distributed ignorance.  And we know and understand less while being incr-
    easingly capable."              Prof. Peter Cochrane, formerly of BT Labs

At 08:20 PM 1/16/2002 -0500, Ron Ackerman writeth:
>I currently have 11 domains running and I am trying to set up a webcam using 
>WebCam2000. WebCam 2000 can be set up for any port and is currently using
port 
>8080. Xitami is set up for default port 80 and needs to stay there. I can
set up 
>the DNS server for webcam.<domain>.com. How should I set up Xitami to
alias port 
>8080 for that subdomain. Any ideas?

Well, you could always use a script to redirect to port 8080.  Here's a
quickie PHP script that will do the trick:

<?
  header("Location: http://webcam.<domain>.com:8080/");
?>


Hope this helps!

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 17 13:29:29 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Pieter Hintjens)
Date: Thu, 17 Jan 2002 14:29:29 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Session context management...
In-Reply-To: <64DB6640B57B4C4B97F5E2A7902494170AB3E5@cawhqexch01.caw.com>
Message-ID: <3C46DFC9.24772.4EC79DD@localhost>

"Joseph Saunders" <jsaunders@caw.com> wrote:

> Ideally when a user is logged on and navigating the GUI, a second user
> could log in and do the same.  Supporting this will require management
> of each user session.

[I've cc'd this answer to xitami-dev, where this discussion can 
continue.]

We've done this before... long time back we wrote a session 
management layer for Xitami.  It was part of our WTP protocol 
handler, a kind of large-scale LRWP manager that we built for our 
Studio toolkit.

WTP is a bit like LRWP but more complex.  We wrote our Studio 
application programs using Libero and the same form i/o system that 
comes with Xitami's administration SDK.  Studio has been static for a 
while and I've now put it into our public CVS archive.

This should be available from:

    http://cvs.imatix.com./cgi-bin/viewcvs/

when the site has been mirrored, which will happen some time today.

Check the OpenKernel Studio directory.  I can't guarantee that Studio 
will make sense or even build.  You will have to be ready to build 
your own version of Xitami (it uses a WSX plugin).

-
Pieter Hintjens
iMatix Corporation

> $filepath_type = $HTTP_POST_FILES["filepath_posted"]["type"];
> if (move_uploaded_file($filepath_on_server, $new_location)) {
>  ...
> }
>
>
>
> marcio

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 17 21:03:45 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 18 Jan 2002 10:03:45 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] File Uploads
In-Reply-To: Message from "Peter" <peterdn@telusplanet.net>
 of "Thu, 17 Jan 2002 13:42:07 PDT." <009301c19f97$6df16820$3c01a8c0@GIA>
Message-ID: <200201172103.KAA01575@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <009301c19f97$6df16820$3c01a8c0@GIA>, "Peter" writes:
>hmmm...  I wonder if the move_upload_file subroutine is part of the cgi.pm
>module.  Do you know?

No I don't think so (it's a PHP thing) -- but there are similar routines
in CGI.pm that work quite well.

As you noted in an earlier mesage, the main thing is that to read binary
files you'll have to tell Perl to access stdin in binary mode (there is
a function to do this).  Then it should work fine.  Although the CGI.pm
interface is easier -- just have a look through the CGI.pm documentation
for details on handling file uploads.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

-----Original Message-----
From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org

At 08:20 PM 1/16/2002 -0500, Ron Ackerman writeth:
>I currently have 11 domains running and I am trying to set up a webcam
using
>WebCam2000. WebCam 2000 can be set up for any port and is currently using
port
>8080. Xitami is set up for default port 80 and needs to stay there. I can
set up
>the DNS server for webcam.<domain>.com. How should I set up Xitami to
alias port
>8080 for that subdomain. Any ideas?

Well, you could always use a script to redirect to port 8080.  Here's a
quickie PHP script that will do the trick:

<?
  header("Location: http://webcam.<domain>.com:8080/");
?>


Hope this helps!

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 17 22:09:21 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)
Date: Thu, 17 Jan 2002 17:09:21 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] webcam
In-Reply-To: <NFBBKNGGELNPLMHPBOCEEEHKCHAA.admin@miplanet.net>
Message-ID: <000701c19fa3$9dbd0260$0100a8c0@celeron2k>

	You can do redirects with regular html, you don't need PHP.

	If you save this file to index.html:


<!DOCTYPE HTML PUBLIC "-//W3C//DTD HTML 4.0 Transitional//EN">
<HTML><HEAD>
<META content="text/html; charset=unicode" http-equiv=Content-Type>
<META content="MSHTML 5.00.2614.3500" name=GENERATOR></HEAD>
<BODY onload="window.location='index.php'"></BODY></HTML>


	and visit it with a browser, it will try to redirect to 'index.php' on the same
host. Just put what you need in there, instead of 'index.php'.


	I am not claiming this is an answer to your original question, I am just saying
you can redirect without having to learn/install PHP.


marcio

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 17 22:04:48 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Craig Morrison)
Date: Thu, 17 Jan 2002 17:04:48 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] webcam
References: <NFBBKNGGELNPLMHPBOCEEEHKCHAA.admin@miplanet.net>
Message-ID: <3C474A80.3A17D360@2cah.com>

miplanet wrote:
> 
> I guess it's time to learn PHP. I have no idea what to do with this. I'll
> start doing some research on this but in the mean time...
> 
> Where do I need to put it to redirect webcam.domain.com to port 8080?

No need to learn PHP (although PHP *is* cool) as HTML already can do this for
you.

A standard HTML anchor will do the trick from a webpage:

 Click <a href="http://webcam.domain.com:8080/">here</a> for the webcam.

If you are wanting to redirect when someone hits a page:

 <META HTTP-EQUIV=Refresh CONTENT="10; URL=http://webcam.domain.com:8080/">

Put the above in the <head></head> section and after 10 seconds most modern
browsers will redirect users automatically.

-- 

Craig Morrison
  http://www.mtsprofessional.com/
  A Win32 Email server that works for you.

	You are getting a PHP error, I sent a tip that does not involve PHP at all. You
must have replied to the wrong msg.

	Now, back to your PHP header problem below, the header line has to be the 1st
line of PHP code to run. Actually it has to be the 1st one that generates
output, but it is usually a good rule of thumb to put it as the 1st line of
code, even before you generate <html> etc etc.

	Just read the PHP manual, about the header function.


marcio

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 17 22:48:33 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (miplanet)
Date: Thu, 17 Jan 2002 17:48:33 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] webcam
In-Reply-To: <3C474A80.3A17D360@2cah.com>
Message-ID: <NFBBKNGGELNPLMHPBOCEOEHLCHAA.admin@miplanet.net>

I think we are a little off track here. The problem is that
webcam.ackerman-family.com points to port 80 via the DNS. The A record for
ackerman-family.com points to internal IP 192.168.1.3, the CNAME point
www.ackerman-famly.com to ackerman-family.com. So any subdomain that is not
defined in the DNS will go to 192.168.1.3 port 80 (80 is opened on the
router and is what Xitami is set for). So port 8080 will not work. I have
even tried opening port 8080 on the router but you can't specify a port in
dns records (that I know of). I think I can have the DNS server point
webcam.ackerman-family.com to a different IP with an A record to that
effect.

You see why I'm so confused.

Oh I can specify a different port for the webcam, I just can't specify an IP
address.

Ron Ackerman

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 17 23:39:31 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (David Holm)
Date: Thu, 17 Jan 2002 16:39:31 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] webcam
References: <NFBBKNGGELNPLMHPBOCEOEHLCHAA.admin@miplanet.net>
Message-ID: <001101c19fb0$366abd70$0b46dacf@rivcom.net>

You can put in a page like www.ackerman-family.com/webcam.html with a meta
redirect to port 8080 something like this:
<META HTTP-EQUIV=Refresh CONTENT="0;
URL=http://webcam.ackerman-family.com:8080/">
Which would point at another copy of Xitami running on port 8080 and
handling the web camera and set that up as a virtual site or in DNS, either
should work. It would probably be easiest to do on a network setup with DNS.
There are many different ways to do this on a network.

David Holm <david.holm@rivcom.net>
System Administrator, River Communications

> dns records (that I know of). I think I can have the DNS server point
> webcam.ackerman-family.com to a different IP with an A record to that
> effect.
>
> You see why I'm so confused.
>
> Oh I can specify a different port for the webcam, I just can't specify an
IP
> address.

-----Original Message-----
From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org
[mailto:xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org]On Behalf Of David Holm
Sent: Thursday, January 17, 2002 6:40 PM
To: xitami@lists.xitami.org
Subject: Re: [Xitami] webcam


You can put in a page like www.ackerman-family.com/webcam.html with a meta
redirect to port 8080 something like this:
<META HTTP-EQUIV=Refresh CONTENT="0;
URL=http://webcam.ackerman-family.com:8080/">
Which would point at another copy of Xitami running on port 8080 and
handling the web camera and set that up as a virtual site or in DNS, either
should work. It would probably be easiest to do on a network setup with DNS.
There are many different ways to do this on a network.

David Holm <david.holm@rivcom.net>
System Administrator, River Communications

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan 18 00:06:39 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Craig Morrison)
Date: Thu, 17 Jan 2002 19:06:39 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] webcam
References: <NFBBKNGGELNPLMHPBOCEOEHLCHAA.admin@miplanet.net>
Message-ID: <3C47670F.835B6043@2cah.com>

Comments below...

miplanet wrote:
> 
> I think we are a little off track here. The problem is that
> webcam.ackerman-family.com points to port 80 via the DNS. The A record for
> ackerman-family.com points to internal IP 192.168.1.3, the CNAME point
> www.ackerman-famly.com to ackerman-family.com. So any subdomain that is not
> defined in the DNS will go to 192.168.1.3 port 80 (80 is opened on the
> router and is what Xitami is set for). So port 8080 will not work. I have
> even tried opening port 8080 on the router but you can't specify a port in
> dns records (that I know of). I think I can have the DNS server point
> webcam.ackerman-family.com to a different IP with an A record to that
> effect.

Your confusion is understood, I was there once myself. DNS has nothing to do
with ports, it only serves to translate a name to an IP address. Your router
takes care of port forwarding and translating between external and internal IP
addresses.

With that in mind, open up port 8080 on your router and have it forwarded to
192.168.1.3. Make sure that webcam.ackerman-family.com points to your
_external_ IP (which it does, nslookup reports that).

Then use one of the redirection techniques that have been suggested on the
list. The following type of redirection will be supported by most modern
browsers (and doesn't require JavaScript):

<META HTTP-EQUIV=Refresh CONTENT="0;
URL=http://webcam.ackerman-family.com:8080/">

Just make sure you place it in the <head> section of your HTML document.

To get to the document, all depends on whether you have virtual domains setup
or not.

If you don't, you just need to create an HTML document with the above in it
and place it in your webpages folder. Which means you'll need a link of some
kind on another page to get to it.

Personally what I would do is put the above in a basic HTML document and save
it as index.html in a folder off the webpages folder, say 'webcam'. So you
would end up with:

\xitami\webpages\webcam

Which could be used as the [Server]webpages entry in the cfg file for a
virtual domain.

Does that help any?

--
Craig Morrison
  http://www.mtsprofessional.com/
  A Win32 Email server that works for you.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan 18 00:47:39 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Thu, 17 Jan 2002 19:47:39 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] webcam
References: <NFBBKNGGELNPLMHPBOCEOEHLCHAA.admin@miplanet.net>
Message-ID: <3C4770AB.7FB4CFE@rci.rutgers.edu>

> I think we are a little off track here. 

Way off track. 

> The problem is that webcam.ackerman-family.com points to port 80 via the DNS. 

Well, no, it doesn't point to port 80; DNS isn't about ports.
Port 80 is assumed by every web browser ever made; but they can
be told to use another port with a URL like domain.com:8080

Therefore your webcam "should" now be working at
http://www.ackerman-family.com:8080

However I get no response. You may have the webcam turned-off at
the moment I tried, or you may be mucking around with overly
complex redirections. And you MUST open port 8080 in your router
or this is never going to work. 

Granted, telling your kin to use :port notation is going to
baffle everybody over age 16. You need a plain URL. 

Is there a reason you want a unique machine name for your webcam?
Or would it be good enough to have a URL like
http://www.ackerman-family.com/webcam ? Webcams are often
embedded in static pages where you can show static info related
to the webcam. 

On that page, have an "image" link like IMG
SRC="http://www.ackerman-family.com:8080" -- however, I'm not
sure that format will work, and can't test it since I can't get
any response from port 8080 at your URL. 

 -PRR

-----Original Message-----
From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org
[mailto:xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org]On Behalf Of Control-Freak
Sent: Thursday, January 10, 2002 1:01 PM
To: xitami@lists.xitami.org
Subject: Re: [Xitami] FW: Website using Xitami


I am not sure that the problem is not much more simple than everyone has
made it, as it has been a couple of days since the original post, and I am
able to connect just fine.  I have had similar problems as I have had other
companies host my sites up until recently.  In trying to find a good
provider, I often moved my site.

I found DNS updating to be a long and slow process.  It always seemed that
within  2 days or so of pointing my Domain at a host IP, half of the
internet could connect to my site, and half couldn't.  It often took more
than 2 weeks before I could trace route my site from servers everwhere (you
can do this at www.tracert.com).

If you have just recently set up your server, and pointed your domain at
your dynamic ISP service, be patient.  I know its very frustrating.  Within
a couple of weeks everyone will probably be able to connect to your site.

Good Luck,

Jay Aldrich

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan 18 12:29:06 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 19 Jan 2002 01:29:06 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] List Help Headers - too much
In-Reply-To: Message from Gordon Wong <gordonw@interchange.ubc.ca>
 of "Thu, 17 Jan 2002 22:24:50 -0800." <3.0.6.32.20020117222450.01a81b50@192.168.2.1>
Message-ID: <200201181229.BAA06004@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3.0.6.32.20020117222450.01a81b50@192.168.2.1>, Gordon Wong writes:
>Can the list administrator move the list help headers somewhere else? I
>can't easliy browse the submissions without scrolling every one.  

They're automatically added by the mailing list software; and can't easily
be moved.  Most mail readers can be configured to display only selected
headers on each message; or not to display selected headers of a
message.  (I typically only display From/To/Subject/Date by default.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan 18 20:31:24 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 18 Jan 2002 15:31:24 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] List Help Headers - too much
References: <3.0.6.32.20020117222450.01a81b50@192.168.2.1>
Message-ID: <3C48861C.316936D7@rci.rutgers.edu>

> move the list help headers somewhere else? I can't easliy browse the submissions without scrolling every one.  
> X-Mailer: QUALCOMM Windows Eudora Light Version 3.0.6 (32)

Eudora, in both version 1.4 (my wife still uses that!) and in
version 4 (a buddy uses that) can hide most headers. I assume
that 3.0.6 can too. 

They used to call the option "Show all headers (even ugly ones)".
I suspect you want to toggle that option OFF, so you don't see
ugly headers. (This list-bot is not the worst I've seen for
flooding the header space.) 

NetScape gives me a 3 way choice. 99% of the time I keep it in
the least-header mode. I turn on All headers only when debugging
clients' emails or tracing spammers. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan 18 20:33:52 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 18 Jan 2002 15:33:52 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] webcam
References: <NFBBKNGGELNPLMHPBOCEGEHNCHAA.admin@miplanet.net>
Message-ID: <3C4886B0.996CA57A@rci.rutgers.edu>

M> I don't have port 8080 turned on for forwarding on the router.
Give it a try now.

CM> Got a nice picture of a chair.. :-)

I see: 

http://www.ackerman-family.com:8080/
 - Picture of chair

http://webcam.ackerman-family.com/
 - stock Xitami home page

Here's a variant hack. Copy the HTML code below to a file. It
works on my machine, pulling the live image from your machine,
and wrapping it in some (bogus) text. It should work well posted
on your machine as a sub-page. Or post it as the index page on
your webcam vHost. 

 <html>
 <head><META HTTP-EQUIV=Refresh CONTENT="10"></head>
 <body bgcolor=#000033>
 <center>
 <font face=arial size=5 color=Yellow>
 Welcome to the home page of</font><br>
 <img src="http://www.ackerman-family.com:8080/" 
  border=0 vspace=14><br>
 <font face=arial size=6 color=Yellow>
 <b>The Invisible Man</b></font><br>
 </center>
 <hr>
 <font face=arial size=2 color=Yellow>
 I think we are a little off track here. 
 webcam.ackerman-family.com points to port 80 via the DNS. 
 <hr>
 Your confusion is understood, I was there once myself. 
 DNS has nothing to do with ports, it only serves to 
 translate a name to an IP address.</font>
 <hr>
 </body>
 </html>

--- Disadvantage: it refreshes the whole page every 10 seconds,
when only the image has changed. If the text were longer and you
scroll to read it, the page jumps back to the top every 10
seconds. A Frame layout might cure that. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jan 19 00:48:45 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Gordon Wong)
Date: Fri, 18 Jan 2002 16:48:45 -0800
Subject: [Xitami] List Help Headers - too much
In-Reply-To: <3C48861C.316936D7@rci.rutgers.edu>
References: <3.0.6.32.20020117222450.01a81b50@192.168.2.1>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20020118164845.0194ea00@192.168.2.1>

There was no switch I could find in Eudora 3 light so I went into the
eudora.ini and added a long line in the [Settings] section.  Now everything
displays cleanly.  Thanks all for pointing me in right direction!

The line so far reads:
TabooHeaders=List-Help,List-Post,List-Subscribe,List-Id,List-Unsubscribe,Lis
t-Archive,Received,Message-ID,X-Authentication-Warning,X-Accept-Language,MIM
E-Version,References,Content-Type,Content-Transfer-Encoding,Errors-To,X-Been
There,X-Mailman-Version,X-MSMail-Priority,X-MIMEOLE,X-MIMETrack,X-Listproces
sor-Version,X-OriginalArrivalTime,X-Priority,X-Sender,Precedence,In-Reply-To
,Content-ID,Content-Disposition,Importance,Delivery-date

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jan 19 08:18:53 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Espen Ruud)
Date: Sat, 19 Jan 2002 09:18:53 +0100
Subject: SV: [Xitami] Virtual Hosts Help
Message-ID: <FB7624FAD451064B9C4E74A807AC7027989C14@ex2000.forus.netpower.no>

I'm not a specialist, but this is how I'm doing this. I currently host about 10 domains on a single IP using the xitami web server.

First of all you need to "point" you domain to the "209.5.45.142" IP in your nameserver, or get your ISP to do this for you.

Then I use the xitami web interface to add a virtual host (click the "virtual host" button and select "new")

1. Enter a name for the ".cfg" file at the top (any name)
2. Select "All addresses" in the IP Address field.
3. Enter your domain name in the DNS field
4. Enter the full path of the location of the web pages.
5. Click the "create" button at the bottom
6. Restart the web server

Finished!

hope this helps!!
Espen
