	I went back and renamed the Xitami.cfg (actually did a copy and rename) to 
defaults. cfg and base host.cfg. Changed the location of the .aut files and rewrote the 
.cfg's to reflect my web site. (After all why reinvent the wheel, modify it!<LOL>) Among the 
changes,I changed the aliases to 
		(first column)	(second column-path)
		 cdrom        		E:\
		cdrom1			F:\

	I could have called them Moe and Larry or anything else, it doesn't matter. 
Also, if the drive was multi partioned, I could have used the same setup.

	Next in my Index.html, I addressed the drives as cdrom or cdrom1. This Xitami 
understood and took me right to the drive I wanted. I found that the .html could be written 
as ;
	<a href="http://the-beast.hn.org/cdrom/main-index.html"></a>
			or
	<a href="cdrom/main-index.html"></a> 
	(NB: Neither line specifies the drive by a letter only as cdrom) I decided to use 
the shorter of the two, I'm lazy.

	Then from another system I went out on the web and tested it and it worked 
fine.

	So I have to thank you again for at least getting me out of the cycle of how to 
address drive E:\...it was getting very frustrating. Sort of like the old BBS days. The 
standing joke was everything worked locally, but not remotely. <LOL>....

	Hope this helps someone else in the future and if there's anyone with some 
more tips for using externals, I'd love to hear from them.

	Eric Hamel
>On the html page are the links constructed as ftp:// or http://
>
>If /webpages is your root folder for your site, can any http access be
>outside of that root folder?  It could be that if the links are accessed via
>http the link could not access outside of your /webpages folder.  Just a
>thought.
>
>Peter

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jan 19 16:51:37 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Sat, 19 Jan 2002 17:51:37 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Logfile question
Message-ID: <46529@dsl.co.uk>

In message <NFBBLAFKPCJBBOJPIMLBKEAGDJAA.hieronymus_schweiz@yahoo.de>
   "Hieronymus" writes:

> Hi Mailinglist

This REALLY needs to be added, fast, to the FAQ (I presume that there IS
an FAQ on the website, and that this matter is not already there?)

> 217.162.161.21 - - [19/Jan/2002:16:28:44 +0100] "GET
> /scripts/..%252f../winnt/system32/cmd.exe?/c+dir HTTP/1.0" 404 0 "" ""
> 
> I have a bunch of error messages in my logfile. What do they mean?

It means that some moron running IIS has allowed his system to be
infected by one of a number of viruses (CodeRed, Nimda, etc) which then
probe the IP address space looking for other idiots also running
unprotected versions of IIS, so that they can infect them also.

It won't hurt Xitami, although if the volume is excessive you might not
like the continuing expansion of your log file.  I would suggest
identifying the ISP(s) of the connecting machine(s) so that you can tell
them, and they in turn can inform their customer.

-- 
Brian {Hamilton Kelly}                                          bhk@dsl.co.uk
    "We have gone from a world of concentrated knowledge and wisdom to one of
    distributed ignorance.  And we know and understand less while being incr-
    easingly capable."              Prof. Peter Cochrane, formerly of BT Labs

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jan 19 20:35:29 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 20 Jan 2002 09:35:29 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Logfile question
In-Reply-To: Message from "Hieronymus" <hieronymus_schweiz@yahoo.de>
 of "Sat, 19 Jan 2002 18:12:03 BST." <NFBBLAFKPCJBBOJPIMLBKEAGDJAA.hieronymus_schweiz@yahoo.de>
Message-ID: <200201192035.JAA25997@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <NFBBLAFKPCJBBOJPIMLBKEAGDJAA.hieronymus_schweiz@yahoo.de>, "Hieronym
us" writes:
>217.162.161.21 - - [19/Jan/2002:16:28:44 +0100] "GET
>/scripts/..%252f../winnt/system32/cmd.exe?/c+dir HTTP/1.0" 404 0 "" ""
>
>I have a bunch of error messages in my logfile. What do they mean?

Someone is attempting to make use of an IIS exploit (or CodeRed/Nimda/etc 
infection; I forget which that exact one is).  Xitami isn't vulnerable
to these, and is saying "not here" in reply to them.  But generally all
the programs trying these automatically don't check for IIS, etc, they
just try the exploit out anyway.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jan 19 22:58:38 2002

In-Reply-To: <FB7624FAD451064B9C4E74A807AC7027989C14@ex2000.forus.netpower.no>

with a static IP that I provide to the vhost?

-----Original Message-----
From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org
[mailto:xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org]On Behalf Of Espen Ruud
Sent: January 19, 2002 3:19 AM
To: xitami@lists.xitami.org
Subject: SV: [Xitami] Virtual Hosts Help


I'm not a specialist, but this is how I'm doing this. I currently host about
10 domains on a single IP using the xitami web server.

First of all you need to "point" you domain to the "209.5.45.142" IP in your
nameserver, or get your ISP to do this for you.

Then I use the xitami web interface to add a virtual host (click the
"virtual host" button and select "new")

1. Enter a name for the ".cfg" file at the top (any name)
2. Select "All addresses" in the IP Address field.
3. Enter your domain name in the DNS field
4. Enter the full path of the location of the web pages.
5. Click the "create" button at the bottom
6. Restart the web server

Finished!

hope this helps!!
Espen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jan 21 08:42:13 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 21 Jan 2002 21:42:13 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] I'm to stupid: Virtual Hosts
In-Reply-To: Message from "Robert M. Muench" <robert.muench@robertmuench.de>
 of "Mon, 21 Jan 2002 09:02:54 BST." <NCBBLHNNKNPMOBPMIBDHCEHCOLAA.robert.muench@robertmuench.de>
Message-ID: <200201210842.VAA01252@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <NCBBLHNNKNPMOBPMIBDHCEHCOLAA.robert.muench@robertmuench.de>, "Robert
 M. Muench" writes:
>1. I have a xitami.cfg and a defaults.cfg file. So IMO Xitami uses the
>defaults.cfg file. My defaults.cfg file looks like this:
>
>[Server]
>    Webpages = "/var/www/html"

Don't sent [Server] webpages in defaults.cfg; due to a bug in Xitami it
will override every other webpages definition.  Set it in basehost.cfg
for the base one, and then in each virtual host instead.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jan 22 04:08:27 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 22 Jan 2002 17:08:27 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] problems with xibuild under OpenBSD
In-Reply-To: Message from Greg Stienstra <greg@videotron.ca>
 of "Mon, 21 Jan 2002 22:42:06 CDT." <3C4CDF8E.F5ADE35A@videotron.ca>
Message-ID: <200201220408.RAA06341@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3C4CDF8E.F5ADE35A@videotron.ca>, Greg Stienstra writes:
>I am unable to get xibuild to work under OpenBSD, it appears OpenBSD makes use
>of an "ar" (object librarian) program of a different lineage than do linux, and
>freebsd, and refuses to do its job if the 's' switch is used.

IIRC "ar s" is a SysVism that the GNU tools also have.  OpenBSD is a BSD
true'n'true, and they tend to use ranlib instead.

The "c" compile script will support this, and it is controlled by the
"RANLIB" variable in the script.  The existing script has an entry for
FreeBSD which does basically this; you probably want to make that one
match OpenBSD too (and presumably NetBSD).

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 24 04:09:38 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 24 Jan 2002 17:09:38 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami on OpenBSD chapter 2...
In-Reply-To: Message from Greg Stienstra <greg@videotron.ca>
 of "Wed, 23 Jan 2002 22:45:47 CDT." <3C4F836B.A5A74F90@videotron.ca>
Message-ID: <200201240409.RAA20944@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3C4F836B.A5A74F90@videotron.ca>, Greg Stienstra writes:
>Compiling sflbits...
>this is c.conf seting up parameters for the imatix c procedure
>ar: creating archive libsfl.a
>ar: sflbits.o;: No such file or directory
>ar: ranlib: No such file or directory

For some reason it appears that the file name is being seen as "sflbits.o;"
which isn't right, and that "ranlib" is being seen as an argument to the
ar command, which also isn't right (ranlib is a command in its own
right).

The command line ought to look something like:

ar r libsfl.a sflbits.o; ranlib libsfl.a

but from the errors that you show it seems like it looks something like
this:

ar r libsfl.a "sflbits.o;" ranlib libsfl.a

which won't work.

I'd suggest finding the line in the script calling "ar", and adding some
echos before it to display what it is running; a common thing that I do
is copy the line and add echo " before it, and " after it. (Although in
this instance that may not show exactly what we want, but it should
point you in the right direction.)

>Could it be that I need to regenerate the 'build' scripts? How?

The error that you show is clearly within the "c" script (which handles
adding the right suffixes to things as it goes), so you don't need to
rebuild the other build scripts.  (Unlike, say, automake/autoconf, the
Makefiles that are generated by otto are pretty generic, with all the
customisation handled in the "c" compile script.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 24 09:47:02 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (KERESZTFALVI Laszlo)
Date: Thu, 24 Jan 2002 10:47:02 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] getting the IP address from a cisco 678 external router
In-Reply-To: <20020124063616.70606.qmail@web13402.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20020124063616.70606.qmail@web13402.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20020124104702.P1922@buci>

On Wed, Jan 23, 2002 at 10:36:16PM -0800, Carl Bartlett wrote:
> How do i get xitami to detect my ip address such that i will open a
> connection on the address of the external router?  Im behind the router
> and am getting ip addresses of 10.0.0.3 and 127.0.0.1 How do i set it up
> so that i can connect to xitami for the ip address given to the router?

I'm not sure I understand appropriately but..

I assume your router does Network Address Translation (NAT). So, the
address at the external end of the router will be forwarded (and
translated) to your machine behind onto the address given by the router.
When you open a connection to the address of your router it will end in
your machine whatever IP address it has got.

Furthermore, You can make any program (and Xitami also) to listen on all
of your interfaces online (ethernet, local:127.0.0.1, ...) pointing it to
0.0.0.0

Hope this helps
Laszlo

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 24 12:26:25 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Bob Paddock)
Date: Thu, 24 Jan 2002 07:26:25 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Security Alert! PHP CGI cannot be accessed directly.
Message-ID: <20020124072662.SM00301@there>


I'm running Xitami on my Linux box, I wanted to try out some PHP scripts and 
I got the following, can some one transliate what it might mean for Xitami 
since it seems to be written fro Apache?:

"Security Alert! PHP CGI cannot be accessed directly.
This PHP CGI binary was compiled with force-cgi-redirect enabled.  This
means that a page will only be served up if the REDIRECT_STATUS CGI variable 
is set.  This variable is set, for example, by Apache's Action directive 
redirect.

You may disable this restriction by recompiling the PHP binary with the
--disable-force-cgi-redirect switch.  If you do this and you have your PHP CGI
binary accessible somewhere in your web tree, people will be able to 
circumvent .htaccess security by loading files through the PHP parser.  A 
good way around this is to define doc_root in your php.ini file to something 
other than your top-level DOCUMENT_ROOT.  This way you can separate the part 
of your web space which uses PHP from the normal part using .htaccess 
security.  If you do not have any .htaccess restrictions anywhere on your 
site you can leave doc_root undefined."

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 24 09:52:47 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Thu, 24 Jan 2002 09:52:47
Subject: [Xitami] Security Alert! PHP CGI cannot be accessed
 directly.
In-Reply-To: <20020124072662.SM00301@there>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20020124095247.00a13ca8@shininglightpro.com>

At 07:26 AM 1/24/2002 -0500, Bob Paddock writeth:
>I'm running Xitami on my Linux box, I wanted to try out some PHP scripts and 
>I got the following, can some one transliate what it might mean for Xitami 
>since it seems to be written fro Apache?:
>
>"Security Alert! PHP CGI cannot be accessed directly.
>This PHP CGI binary was compiled with force-cgi-redirect enabled.  This
>means that a page will only be served up if the REDIRECT_STATUS CGI variable 
>is set.  This variable is set, for example, by Apache's Action directive 
>redirect.

This probably suggests that you were, at one time, running PHP from Apache.
 Apache sets the REDIRECT_STATUS CGI variable when it executes the PHP
binary.  You have two options:

1)  Recompile the PHP binary by following the rest of the directions.  This
may or may not be acceptable depending on whether other users on the system
are allowed to use PHP from the command-line.

2)  Create a wrapper program/Perl script for PHP that sets the
REDIRECT_STATUS environment variable.  Then point Xitami at the wrapper
program instead of at PHP.

Hope this helps!


          Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@shininglightpro.com
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

I'm making an assumtion here so correct me if I am wrong ...
I am assumming you already have http://domain.com working with Xitami.

You can use a virtual host to do this if you like....
As long as you are looking for it to point to the same machine.
from the administration utility select virtual hosts, new, enter a config
name, enter the url something.domain.com on the DNS entry line
and point to the respective directories to point to.
Vance

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan 25 17:16:11 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 25 Jan 2002 12:16:11 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] How to???
References: <004301c1a4d2$e76aad20$0200a8c0@wolfpower>
Message-ID: <3C5192DB.1E718B4@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  If domain = http://domain.com
> How do I set up something like this?
> http://something.domain.com

Ask your ISP's DNS administrator to set up an alias (or CNAME) of
something.domain.com that points to domain.com. 

A default installation of Xitami does not care what name is used to request
pages-- if a request comes to it, it serves its default page. 

If your real question is: how to make something.domain.com show a different
page than domain.com..... use the vHost wizard in Xitami's Admin screens. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jan 25 17:26:14 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Vance Forste)
Date: Fri, 25 Jan 2002 12:26:14 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] percent chars in the url
References: <85046AFB36C9D3118F520008C72BBEE405C51B4C@HOUXML05>
Message-ID: <018a01c1a5c5$64123620$2c838282@vance2>

The percent sign indicates the next 2 characters are for the hexidecimal
value of the character in the URL. For instance if you find a %20 it means
there is a space in the URL or one of the files you are pointing to....
Remove the space from the filename and it will fix it. However in your case
%2E is a period .... Your browser should have no problems interpreting this.
I don't believe this is a problem with xitami...
Just a shot in the dark, but check to see if pdf is a valid mime type in
xitami.. if not try adding it. see if this resolves the problem.

Vance

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jan 27 06:20:05 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Joe Byrne)
Date: Sun, 27 Jan 2002 00:20:05 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] WWW Xitami
References: <001e01c1a6f0$eb45da30$2802a8c0@dougxp> <003601c1a6f4$011fd920$f6fea8c0@jjb> <000701c1a6f7$f110fd80$2802a8c0@dougxp>
Message-ID: <003e01c1a6fa$b8882710$f6fea8c0@jjb>

Doug,
    Cable companies are notorious for locking you into their way of
thinking.  ISP who offer DSL on the other hand generally understand the user
mind set.  Part of my business is offering access via DSL and we have a
large number of companies running web, email, ftp, IRC servers .... just to
name a few.
    I would strongly argue your reasoning about Xitami however.  With modern
software, just because there is no license fee doesn't make the product
inferior.  In fact, I have contracts in excess of $45,000 p/month for
ecommerce web hosting....ALL of which run on 3 servers using Xitami.  I had
MS IIS for awhile, but keeping up with security patches and doing the
necessary housekeeping to keep the damn things running 24x7 became a
full-time job.  To be honest, one of my Web servers (running on Win2k
professional) hasn't been touched for 6 weeks now.  That's a big deal to me.
I know I could run it on *nix and probably not touch them for multiple
months on end, but I also write custom software that only runs on the Win32
system.

--Joe

> > I'd probably use something more substantial than Xitami, wouldn't I?

Matter of taste. IIS has some MS-specific frills, and Apache has
some features good for very high traffic. But a majority of
servers running IIS or Apache could just as well run Xitami. It
is mighty "substantial", mainly by being lean and clean and doing
what it does very well. 

> one of my Web servers (running on Win2k professional) hasn't been touched for 6 weeks now.  That's a big deal to me.

My Xitami 2.49 on WinNT4 has been up since 20 Sept 2001, and was
down then only for a major hardware replacement. If not for some
small bug in FTP upload, that locks it once or twice a year when
one of my helpers tries to upload a mess of files, it would
probably run forever. Especially on Win2000, which has a better
TCP stack than NT4. 

 -PRR

Internet  --CableModem  ---- Server(NIC1)

right?

a) The workings of Xitami?
b) The OS; Win98?
c) Sygate?
d) Something funny the ISP has done to the CableModem?

For one thing..if you're behind a router/firewall/NAT..you can't access =
your
network via public IP...it just won't work..don't try it.

As far as running a web server on residential accounts...cable companies
tend to not allow this because of a few reasons, which I'll try to =
explain
below to the best of my knowledge.

I know @home had very strict policies about servers period. They worked =
on
the idea that not everyone in each neighborhood who subscribed to cable =
was
going to use it (some places had neighborhoods, we had the entire =
county) at
the same time. So, they could wire a t1 to 200 people assuming that only =
20
or so would be on at once. The uplink was capped to prevent too much was
being used.

So if you had 3 or 4 users running servers getting a lot of traffic..it
slowed EVERYONE down.

With DSL it's a bit different..you pay for your bandwidth, and that's =
yours.
Granted the telephone company may have a t3 going to the main =
servers...they
get more if they need it. Some providers kick you off DSL.

I'm a Verizon subscriber. I have a standard 768/128 ADSL Residential
account. I currently run Xitami, M-Daemon Pro, and Serve-U Pro on my =
other
PC upstairs. Now..I have two IP addresses thanks to my hub and DHCP, so =
I am
able to visit my site via public IP and vhosts. I guess I'm just a lucky
one.

http://dewdude.ath.cx

Wow!  That's great!  I don't believe I've ever seen an NT box run longer
than 10 weeks without needing a reboot.  I've never had an issue with Xitami
causing system problems (although I do tend to think the NT Service version
isn't nearly as stable as the Console version).  I do have a regular

those times I'm just asking for trouble.  I also have 3 Netware boxes that
I'm pretty sure have been running non-stop for nearly a year.  18 months ago
I finally took down a 486 Netware v3.12 server that had run non-stop for 3
1/2 years, doing daily file and print sharing.  'Twill be interesting to see
what happens with Netware 6.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jan 27 20:29:51 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Warren 'Llama' Ernst)
Date: Sun, 27 Jan 2002 12:29:51 -0800
Subject: [Xitami] TCP stack problem on windows?
In-Reply-To: <2212886135.20020127185835@chello.nl>
Message-ID: <LKBBKLDHICNIAKJMKNCECEODDLAA.warren@warrenernst.com>

Melle,

My gut reaction here is that Sygate is the "problem." I have a lot of
experience with Sygate AND Xitami on a Win98 box. Whenever I use Sygate as a
NAT (connection sharer), any servers (software daemons, and not just Xitami)
run in that machine act strangely ONLY when you try to access them from a
LOCAL machine.

What I THINK is happeneing here is that Sygate is tring to redirect the
incoming request out to the Internet, but only after some time passes does
it figure out that the request is actually intended for ITSELF, and then let
it through. In so figuring out what to do, Sygate sort of goes beserk for a
little bit, and fails as a NAT until it regains its composure.

There are plenty of solutions. Personally, for the home office, I have been
using a Linksys DSL-Router for NAT duties. It is much more stable than
sygate, more flexible for port forwarding, and it never requires rebooting
;-). With Sygate off of your Win98 server, it can be free to run Xitami
quite happily. Just tell the Router to forward port 80 (and port 21, if
using FTP also) to the Xitami machine.

I have a Win98 machine running Xitami, a separate FTP server, a mail server
(pop and SMTP), a remote access server (sort of like PC Anywhere), plus it
serves out a laser printer to the LAN and provides a shared Windows hard
drive. I restart it every 80 days just out of habit. Though it is not being
slammed by hundreds of users daily, serving speed is NOT an issue, nor is
stability. And this is a Pentium 133 with around 80 megs of ram I'm talking
about here.

My point here is to say that Win98 can be fine for your server if there
aren't dozens of concurrent users slamming it.

-Warr

Melle Koning wrote:
> 
> So, the server has two NICs, one for the 'outside' and the other for
> the Lan. The server runs Win98 and serves my homepage with Xitami.

Win98 never has handled multiple NICs very well.

You'd be better off buying a broadband router/switch. That way you can use a
single NIC connected to the router/switch that will allow you access to
internet and your local LAN.

I just wrote to another post on this email list that I reboot my *Win98*
server every 80 days as a preventative measure only. It runs Xitami, WarFTP,
a remote access server (like PC Anywhere), a SMTP/POP server, Norton AV
weekly, PHP, plus it serves out a laser printer to the LAN and provides
shared Windows hard drive space.

True, it only services 5 people plus my LAN and elsewhere, about 300 emails
a day, and less than 50 unique web visitors daily, but it has been much
easier to manage and more secure than Mandrake 7 & 8, RedHat 6, NT4, or
2KPro. I'm sure it wouldn't scale that well, but for this, it works great.

-Warr

I've run my win2k box for much longer periods of time and once everything is
configured properly, there should be NO reason it should go down. When I was
running my server at my college, it was up for about 7 or so months before we
had a power outage that lasted for over 3 hours (my apc only lasts 1 hour or
so).

The best thing about an NT or 2K box is that you can run everything as a service
so if the power does go out, you can always be assured when it ome back on that
everything can be restores back to the norm.

-Evan

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jan 27 22:03:11 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Control-Freak)
Date: Sun, 27 Jan 2002 17:03:11 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] WWW Xitami
References: <LKBBKLDHICNIAKJMKNCEMEODDLAA.warren@warrenernst.com>
Message-ID: <014101c1a77e$6b4e5c60$b61e2341@concentric.net>

I'm really bad.  I run xitami (web server and ftp service) in the background
on a ME machine that is constantly being used as a multi-track digital audio
workstation.  Most people would call me an idiot, but until i get time to
dig enough parts out of the closet to make something like a pentium pro 200
MHz dedicated server, it works just fine for me.  It crashes every once in a
great while, but no more than it did when it was a dedicated DAW.  Running
Xitami in the background doesn't seem to impede performance at all.  And
some of the files i serve are over 10 meg.

 But, I do have to admit that I am running a AMD Athelon 1.4GHz 233 FSB with
256Meg DDR PC2100 RAM off a 7200 RPM ATA66 HD.  But most of those resources
get eaten up by the DAW side of things anyway (hence the crashes).  But even
as a daw/ web server, its far more stable than my p.o.s. dedicated office
computer (Dell Inspiron 3800 MPIII750 with 256 PC100 RAM - Dell, please come
home.) that crashes 2 or 3 times a day due to eaten up resources - even with
a memory manager (AnalogX's MaxMem).

- Jay Aldrich

You need the Service version, you need to be Administrator. The self-installer
may fail; open a DOS box, switch to the Xitami directory, and run "xiwinnt -i"
to bind it to the Windows Service manager.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jan 28 22:13:43 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Control-Freak)
Date: Mon, 28 Jan 2002 17:13:43 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] port address
References: <web-391349@sesslerford.com> <OE57w0jU8SErS3q6uHb0000dec8@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <008701c1a849$107708c0$b61e2341@concentric.net>

Use dns2go from www.dns2go.com .  Its free, and it optionally does automatic
port forwarding for anything with a www. prefix in front.  So, your site
would be http://www.mysite.com, and your ftp would be ftp://mysite.com .  I
have yet to figure out a way to get ftp://www.mysite.com to work, but I
think that is because it forwards anything with www. in it to the port you
specify, so the ftp request is not sent to the proper port.  I have to admit
that I haven't spent much time on it, so there my still be a way to do it.

Jay Aldrich

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jan 29 14:54:21 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)
Date: Tue, 29 Jan 2002 09:54:21 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] xitami - php (PHP_SELF)
In-Reply-To: <16VYG0-0TGbjsC@fmrl02.sul.t-online.com>
Message-ID: <001e01c1a8d4$d5ea9be0$0100a8c0@celeron2k>

> When running the phpinfo() to get all the values for the system
> variables etc ... the PHP_SELF variable is blank/empty .... it should
> normally return the URL of the webpage from where you call the
> phpinfo () function or the variable itself.
> 
> Anyone have an idea where the mistake might be? some Xitami server
> setting somewhere? perhaps a setting in the php.ini configuration?
> Any help is much appreciated. Thanks!
> God bless you with His grace and peace 


	This is what I use:

// Under Apache $PHP_SELF is what we want, under Xitami it is $SCRIPT_NAME
// We find out based on which one has ".php" in it.
if (ereg ("\.php", $SCRIPT_NAME)) $CONSTANT_SELF = $SCRIPT_NAME;
else $CONSTANT_SELF = $PHP_SELF;
$CONSTANT_SELF = str_replace ("\\\\", "/", $CONSTANT_SELF);



	Then just use $CONSTANT_SELF

marcio

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jan 26 14:03:54 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Sat, 26 Jan 2002 15:03:54 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] percent chars in the url
References: <85046AFB36C9D3118F520008C72BBEE405C51B35@HOUXML05>
Message-ID: <3C52B74A.6000408@freesbee.fr>

Brinkle, Jason wrote:

>How do I get rid of those percent signs in the url?
>Example:  http://10.191.32.111/@site/irps/omniweb/005501/planmenu%2Epdf
><http://10.191.32.111/@site/irps/omniweb/005501/planmenu%2Epdf> 
>
If you are refering to links created by Xitami when you view directories 
on the server then the answer is to edit the file template/httpdir.gsl

replace the line
<A HREF="$(urlbase:)$(nameurl:)"><IMG SRC="$(icon)" 
BORDER=0>$(name:)</A></TD>
with the line
<A HREF="$(urlbase:)$(name:)"><IMG SRC="$(icon)" BORDER=0>$(name:)</A></TD>

You may also want to add the following lines near the start (before the 
lines that say
.-  We want the first character of the sort order
.directory.order = substr (order,0,,1) )
This fix allows your users to reverse sort the directory correctly

.- Bug fix - remove leading '=' from directory.order if present
.-  The attribute directory.order has a leading '=' if it is not the 
default
.-  order. For example:
.-  If the order in Xitami's defaults.cfg is 'nx' then when you execute the
.-  gsl for 'http://localhost/directory/' then directory.order is 'nx'
.-  but if you then click on the URL for Size and thus execute gsl for
.-  'http://localhost/directory/?order=snx' then directory.order is '=snx'
.if substr (order,0,,1) = "="
.  order = substr (order,1,,)
.endif
.- End bug fix - remove leading '=' from directory.order if present

   "Edward Willliams" writes:

I hope that if you do implement this, you will be ensuring that any
recipient to whom you send such mail is happy to receive it.  Most people
dislike intensely having HTML sent to them in mail (not least from the
security aspect).

Most definitely HTML never belongs in any mailing-list (or newsgroup)
postings.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jan 30 02:52:24 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 30 Jan 2002 15:52:24 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Associating .cgi with python
In-Reply-To: Message from abulka@netspace.net.au
 of "Wed, 30 Jan 2002 13:44:03 +1100." <1012358643.3c575df371900@webmail.netspace.net.au>
Message-ID: <200201300252.PAA02088@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <1012358643.3c575df371900@webmail.netspace.net.au>, abulka@netspace.n
et.au writes:
>#!/usr/bin/python2
>as the first line of the script, but that only makes sense on my linux machine.
>How do I associate .cgi with python, for Xitami running under windows?

The same way.  Put the #! line in, and then make sure Python is on the
PATH.  Providing you have python2.exe somewhere on your PATH, it'll
"just work" with Xitami.  (Yes, this is a special feature of Xitami.)

Ewen

right track.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jan 30 19:15:16 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Mike Wilson)
Date: Wed, 30 Jan 2002 11:15:16 -0800
Subject: [Xitami] FTP
References: <002901c1a99e$707dbce0$29d235d8@suncoast>
Message-ID: <001501c1a9c2$73c00c40$6501a8c0@ameritech.net>

I had the same recently Dave, I'm new to this server..
Don't rely on browser ftp, use a third party ftp software and make sure
you're set to "passive" mode.
You should get in as Guest with no pass or Aonymouse.  Hunt down the ftp
link under configuration and you can see permissions or create new
permissions.  From there, hit the help button for more info.

Try SmartFTP, it free and fairly full featured.

M. Wilson

p.s Dave

In your linksys, you should be able to drop the DMZ if your not gaming or
webcam and just go to the IP forwarding menu in lynksis admin and set the
ports 80 and 21 open to the machine IP address your hosting with.  This way
your IP address will be less available for exploit on the remaining ports.

Mike

you to do. It works a treat!

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jan 30 17:34:47 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Wed, 30 Jan 2002 12:34:47 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Associating .cgi with python
References: <1012358643.3c575df371900@webmail.netspace.net.au>
Message-ID: <3C582EB7.C7593916@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Under windows, I want Xitami to run .cgi scripts as python script.  I have #!/usr/bin/python2 as the first line of the script, but that only makes sense on my linux machine. How do I associate .cgi with python, for Xitami running under windows?

In Xitami Filters, associate ".cgi" with "C:/snakes/python/python.exe"

Any time Xitami is asked to deliver a file with ".cgi" extension, it will feed
that file through that program, capture the output, and send it to the
browser. 

I don't handle snakes but I do this for a VisualBasic program that processes
database tags in files. In my Xitami Filters, ".htmwl" is associated with
"D:/cgi/fetch.exe", the name of my VB program. 

Alternatively: hack the open-source code for Xitami, find the special-case
where Xitami/Win looks for "#!....perl" as the first line of a file and
searches PATH for a copy of perl.exe, and add similar lines to look for
"#!...python" and search PATH for python.exe. But recompiling Xitami on
Windows seems to want an MS C compiler, and IIRC the GUI version needs a
commercial package so isn't totally "free". 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jan 30 18:27:03 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Craig Morrison)
Date: Wed, 30 Jan 2002 13:27:03 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] FTP
References: <002901c1a99e$707dbce0$29d235d8@suncoast>
Message-ID: <3C583AF7.A34B1282@2cah.com>

Dave Oshel wrote:
> 
> PASV
> 227 Entering Passive Mode (192,168,1,100,0,25)
> connecting to 192.168.1.100:25
> - -
> connecting to 192.168.1.100:25
> Connected to 192.168.1.100 port 25

Hmmm.. Are you running a mail server on this machine?

Port 25 is the standard port for SMTP traffic, Xitami shouldn't be scanning
this low by default. In defaults.cfg add this:

[Ftp]
    data-port=1024

And see what happens.

-- 

Craig Morrison
  http://www.mtsprofessional.com/
  A Win32 Email server that works for you.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jan 30 20:40:07 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 31 Jan 2002 09:40:07 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Associating .cgi with python
In-Reply-To: Message from Paul Reid <preid@rci.rutgers.edu>
 of "Wed, 30 Jan 2002 12:34:47 CDT." <3C582EB7.C7593916@rci.rutgers.edu>
Message-ID: <200201302040.JAA03465@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3C582EB7.C7593916@rci.rutgers.edu>, Paul Reid writes:
>Alternatively: hack the open-source code for Xitami, find the special-case
>where Xitami/Win looks for "#!....perl" as the first line of a file and
>searches PATH for a copy of perl.exe, 

What special case would this be?

The code in sflproc*.* looks for a #! line that is something like:

#! /path/path/executablename flags

and if it can't find the literal /path/path/executablename, it then
takes just the executablename and tries to find that on the path.

It should work fine with Python.

>and add similar lines to look for "#!...python" and search PATH for 
>python.exe. But recompiling Xitami on Windows seems to want an MS C 
>compiler, and IIRC the GUI version needs a commercial package so isn't 
>totally "free". 

You can rebuild the GUI version from source with MSVC.  I guess that
counts as needing a "commercial package", but it's a reasonably widely
available one.  (The source to the GUI was merged into the open source
version with 2.4b9/2.5b5.)

In theory it should be possible to compile it with other compilers, but
particularly the GUI version would take a bit of work to get the
resources compiled properly and linked in.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 31 06:57:32 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Thu, 31 Jan 2002 07:57:32 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] FTP
Message-ID: <46715@dsl.co.uk>

In message <006701c1a9f5$d41f3060$6401a8c0@vance> "Vance Forste" writes:

> Actually the documentaion does claim to support passive mode but I have
> tried it on a few versions and none of them work using passive mode... As a
> matter of fact I get an Invalid command response from it....
> 
> <clip>
> ftp> PASV
> Invalid command.
> </clip>
> Go figure...

Doh!

PASV (and all those other "four-letter" commands, like USER) are the
commands used over the sockets connection between the FTP client and the
FTP server.  Few FTP clients will accept such commands at their user CLI.
These commands are what actually /constitute/ the protocol itself.

Some FTP clients will recognize a QUOTE command, which can push a
complete File Transfer Protocol (guess why I wrote that in full) command
over to the server for execution.

Anyway, the long and short of it is that to take advantage of an FTP
server, like Xitami, which supports "passive FTP" requires that you have
a client that utilizes passive FTP.  

I don't know, for instance, whether the command-line client included in
Windoze uses it: that code (as can be seen by extracting the Copyright
string from the executable) is based upon old BSD code of 1983 vintage.
Is that what you were using above, generating the "ftp> " prompt?

--

Doh is right...
I was not even thinking about that.... I just realized that was the fix and
went on with my business  (I have no use for it...)
Yes it would be a prompt from a Win2K box ....Well in short the defnition of
passive mode is quite simply telling the server that the client will attempt
to establish the file transfer port. It is a server and client command. The
reason passive mode is not working is your firewall is blocking the incoming
port from the client.....
I have to retract my statement earlier Xitami does support passive mode....
Vance

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jan 31 21:26:13 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)

In-Reply-To: Message from "Just" <Just40Fun@hotmail.com>

Message-ID: <200201312126.KAA11683@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <OE61zCOegJuAnY8QYFg0000368c@hotmail.com>, "Just" writes:
>password is correct, the page shows.  However, if wrong info was entered or
>clicked enter with no info was entered, a page showing : "Error processing
>failed - problem with schema" will show while the address still showing the
>original requested URL!  

I take it you're using a 2.5 beta version (you don't say, but that
message shouldn't occur at all with anything earlier).  If so the issue
is that error messages are handled by a GSL template, precisely so you
can customise them.  But for some reason the template cannot be
processed.

Going out on a limb, I'd say you're probably trying to use Xitami 2.5b1
or Xitami 2.5b4 NT service (which is actually 2.5b1 in disguise).  Try
Xitami 2.5b5 (the latest beta) from http://www.xitami.com/

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com
